class="gallerytext">\n<p><a href="/wiki/Woluwe_Saint-Pierre" class="mw-redirect" title="Woluwe Saint-Pierre">Woluwe Saint-Pierre / Sint-Pieters-Woluwe</a>\n</p>\n\t\t\t</div>\n\t\t</div></li>\n</ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Brussels-Capital_Region">Brussels-Capital Region</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brussels&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Brussels-Capital Region">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Regions_of_Belgium.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Regions_of_Belgium.svg/220px-Regions_of_Belgium.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="180" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Regions_of_Belgium.svg/330px-Regions_of_Belgium.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Regions_of_Belgium.svg/440px-Regions_of_Belgium.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="307" data-file-height="251" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Regions_of_Belgium.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Regions of Belgium: <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r981673959">.mw-parser-output .legend{page-break-inside:avoid;break-inside:avoid-column}.mw-parser-output .legend-color{display:inline-block;min-width:1.25em;height:1.25em;line-height:1.25;margin:1px 0;text-align:center;border:1px solid black;background-color:transparent;color:black}.mw-parser-output .legend-text{}</style><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color" style="background-color:#fab274; color:black;">&#160;</span>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Flemish_Region" title="Flemish Region">Flemish Region</a></div><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color" style="background-color:#2385d2; color:black;">&#160;</span>&#160;Brussels-Capital Region</div><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color" style="background-color:#f2536b; color:black;">&#160;</span>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Wallonia" title="Wallonia">Walloon Region</a></div></div></div></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Political_status">Political status</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brussels&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Political status">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Partition_of_Belgium#Brussels" title="Partition of Belgium">Partition of Belgium \xc2\xa7&#160;Brussels</a>; and <a href="/wiki/Communities,_regions_and_language_areas_of_Belgium#Brussels" title="Communities, regions and language areas of Belgium">Communities, regions and language areas of Belgium \xc2\xa7&#160;Brussels</a></div><p>The Brussels-Capital Region is one of the three federated regions of Belgium, alongside the <a href="/wiki/Wallonia" title="Wallonia">Walloon Region</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Flemish_Region" title="Flemish Region">Flemish Region</a>. Geographically and linguistically, it is a bilingual <a href="/wiki/Enclave" class="mw-redirect" title="Enclave">enclave</a> in the monolingual Flemish Region. Regions are one component of Belgium\'s institutions; the three communities being the other component. Brussels\' inhabitants deal with either the <a href="/wiki/French_Community_of_Belgium" title="French Community of Belgium">French Community</a> or the <a href="/wiki/Flemish_Community" title="Flemish Community">Flemish Community</a> for matters such as culture and education, as well as a <a href="/wiki/Common_Community_Commission" title="Common Community Commission">Common Community</a> for competencies which do not belong exclusively to either Community, such as healthcare and social <a href="/wiki/Welfare" title="Welfare">welfare</a>.\n</p><p>Since the split of <a href="/wiki/Brabant_(province)" class="mw-redirect" title="Brabant (province)">Brabant</a> in 1995, the Brussels Region does not belong to any of the <a href="/wiki/Provinces_of_Belgium" title="Provinces of Belgium">provinces of Belgium</a>, nor is it subdivided into provinces itself. Within the Region, 99% of the areas of provincial jurisdiction are assumed by the Brussels regional institutions and community commissions. Remaining is only the <a href="/wiki/Governor_of_Brussels-Capital" class="mw-redirect" title="Governor of Brussels-Capital">governor of Brussels-Capital</a> and some aides, analogously to provinces. Its status is roughly akin to that of a <a href="/wiki/Federal_district" title="Federal district">federal district</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Institutions">Institutions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brussels&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Institutions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Government_of_the_Brussels-Capital_Region" class="mw-redirect" title="Government of the Brussels-Capital Region">Government of the Brussels-Capital Region</a> and <a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_the_Brussels-Capital_Region" title="Parliament of the Brussels-Capital Region">Parliament of the Brussels-Capital Region</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Parlement_r%C3%A9gion_Bruxelles-Capitale.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Parlement_r%C3%A9gion_Bruxelles-Capitale.JPG/220px-Parlement_r%C3%A9gion_Bruxelles-Capitale.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Parlement_r%C3%A9gion_Bruxelles-Capitale.JPG/330px-Parlement_r%C3%A9gion_Bruxelles-Capitale.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Parlement_r%C3%A9gion_Bruxelles-Capitale.JPG/440px-Parlement_r%C3%A9gion_Bruxelles-Capitale.JPG 2x" data-file-width="4272" data-file-height="2848" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Parlement_r%C3%A9gion_Bruxelles-Capitale.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Brussels_Parliament_building" title="Brussels Parliament building">Brussels Parliament building</a></div></div></div>\n<p>The Brussels-Capital Region is governed by a <a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_the_Brussels-Capital_Region" title="Parliament of the Brussels-Capital Region">parliament</a> of 89 members (72 French-speaking, 17 Dutch-speaking\xe2\x80\x94parties are organised on a linguistic basis) and an eight-member regional cabinet consisting of a <a href="/wiki/Minister-President_of_the_Brussels-Capital_Region" title="Minister-President of the Brussels-Capital Region">minister-president</a>, four ministers and three <a href="/wiki/Secretary_of_state" title="Secretary of state">state secretaries</a>. By law, the cabinet must comprise two French-speaking and two Dutch-speaking ministers, one Dutch-speaking secretary of state and two French-speaking secretaries of state. The minister-president does not count against the language quota, but in practice every minister-president has been a bilingual francophone. The regional parliament can enact <a href="/wiki/Ordinance_(Belgium)" title="Ordinance (Belgium)">ordinances</a> (French: <i lang="fr" title="French-language text">ordonnances</i>, Dutch: <i lang="nl" title="Dutch-language text">ordonnanties</i>), which have equal status as a national legislative act.\n</p><p>19 of the 72 French-speaking members of the Brussels Parliament are also members of the <a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_the_French_Community_of_Belgium" class="mw-redirect" title="Parliament of the French Community of Belgium">Parliament of the French Community of Belgium</a>, and, until 2004, this was also the case for six Dutch-speaking members, who were at the same time members of the <a href="/wiki/Flemish_Parliament" title="Flemish Parliament">Flemish Parliament</a>. Now, people voting for a Flemish party have to vote separately for 6 directly elected members of the Flemish Parliament.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Agglomeration_of_Brussels">Agglomeration of Brussels</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brussels&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Agglomeration of Brussels">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Before the creation of the Brussels-Capital Region, regional competences in the 19 municipalities were performed by the Brussels Agglomeration. The Brussels Agglomeration was an administrative division established in 1971. This decentralised administrative public body also assumed jurisdiction over areas which, elsewhere in Belgium, were exercised by municipalities or provinces.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Brussels Agglomeration had a separate legislative council, but the by-laws enacted by it did not have the status of a legislative act. The only election of the council took place on 21 November 1971. The working of the council was subject to many difficulties caused by the linguistic and socio-economic tensions between the two communities.\n</p><p>After the creation of the Brussels-Capital Region, the Brussels Agglomeration was never formally abolished, although it no longer has a purpose.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="French_and_Flemish_communities">French and Flemish communities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brussels&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: French and Flemish communities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/French_Community_Commission" title="French Community Commission">French Community Commission</a> and <a href="/wiki/Flemish_Community_Commission" title="Flemish Community Commission">Flemish Community Commission</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Communities_of_Belgium.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Communities_of_Belgium.svg/220px-Communities_of_Belgium.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="180" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Communities_of_Belgium.svg/330px-Communities_of_Belgium.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Communities_of_Belgium.svg/440px-Communities_of_Belgium.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="307" data-file-height="251" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Communities_of_Belgium.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Communities of Belgium: <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color" style="background-color:#fab274; color:black;">&#160;</span>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Flemish_Community" title="Flemish Community">Flemish Community</a> / Dutch language area</div><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color" style="background-color:#f2536b;"><span style="display:inline-block; width:0; height:0;border-left: 1.25em solid #fab274;border-bottom: 1.25em solid #f2536b;">&#160;</span></span>&#160;Flemish &amp; French Community / bilingual language area</div><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color" style="background-color:#f2536b; color:black;">&#160;</span>&#160;<a href="/wiki/French_Community_of_Belgium" title="French Community of Belgium">French Community</a> / French language area</div><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color" style="background-color:#40bb6a; color:black;">&#160;</span>&#160;<a href="/wiki/German-speaking_Community_of_Belgium" title="German-speaking Community of Belgium">German-speaking Community</a> / German language area</div></div></div></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/French_Community_of_Belgium" title="French Community of Belgium">French Community</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Flemish_Community" title="Flemish Community">Flemish Community</a> exercise their powers in Brussels through two community-specific public authorities: the <a href="/wiki/French_Community_Commission" title="French Community Commission">French Community Commission</a> (French: <i lang="fr" title="French-language text">Commission communautaire fran\xc3\xa7aise</i> or COCOF) and the <a href="/wiki/Flemish_Community_Commission" title="Flemish Community Commission">Flemish Community Commission</a> (Dutch: <i lang="nl" title="Dutch-language text">Vlaamse Gemeenschapscommissie</i> or VGC). These two bodies each have an assembly composed of the members of each linguistic group of the <a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_the_Brussels-Capital_Region" title="Parliament of the Brussels-Capital Region">Parliament of the Brussels-Capital Region</a>. They also have a board composed of the ministers and secretaries of state of each linguistic group in the Government of the Brussels-Capital Region.\n</p><p>The French Community Commission has also another capacity: some legislative powers of the French Community have been devolved to the Walloon Region (for the French language area of Belgium) and to the French Community Commission (for the bilingual language area).<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup> The Flemish Community, however, did the opposite; it merged the Flemish Region into the Flemish Community.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup> This is related to different conceptions in the two communities, one focusing more on the Communities and the other more on the Regions, causing an asymmetrical <a href="/wiki/Federalism" title="Federalism">federalism</a>. Because of this devolution, the French Community Commission can enact <a href="/wiki/Decree" title="Decree">decrees</a>, which are legislative acts.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Common_Community_Commission">Common Community Commission</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brussels&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Common Community Commission">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>A bi-communitarian public authority, the <a href="/wiki/Common_Community_Commission" title="Common Community Commission">Common Community Commission</a> (French: <i lang="fr" title="French-language text">Commission communautaire commune</i>, COCOM, Dutch: <i lang="nl" title="Dutch-language text">Gemeenschappelijke Gemeenschapscommissie</i>, GGC) also exists. Its assembly is composed of the members of the regional parliament, and its board are the ministers\xe2\x80\x94not the secretaries of state\xe2\x80\x94of the region, with the minister-president not having the right to vote. This commission has two capacities: it is a decentralised administrative public body, responsible for implementing cultural policies of common interest. It can give subsidies and enact <a href="/wiki/By-law" title="By-law">by-laws</a>. In another capacity, it can also enact ordinances, which have equal status as a national legislative act, in the field of the welfare powers of the communities: in the Brussels-Capital Region, both the French Community and the Flemish Community can exercise powers in the field of welfare, but only in regard to institutions that are unilingual (for example, a private French-speaking retirement home or the Dutch-speaking hospital of the <a href="/wiki/Vrije_Universiteit_Brussel" title="Vrije Universiteit Brussel">Vrije Universiteit Brussel</a>). The Common Community Commission is responsible for policies aiming directly at private persons or at bilingual institutions (for example, the centres for social welfare of the 19 municipalities). Its ordinances have to be enacted with a majority in both linguistic groups. Failing such a majority, a new vote can be held, where a majority of at least one third in each linguistic group is sufficient.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="International_institutions">International institutions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brussels&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: International institutions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Brussels has, since <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>, become the administrative centre of many international organisations. The <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> (EU) and the <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">North Atlantic Treaty Organisation</a> (NATO) have their main institutions in the city, along with many other international organisations such as the <a href="/wiki/World_Customs_Organization" title="World Customs Organization">World Customs Organization</a> and <a href="/wiki/EUROCONTROL" class="mw-redirect" title="EUROCONTROL">EUROCONTROL</a>, as well as international corporations. Brussels is third in the number of international conferences it hosts,<sup id="cite_ref-ULB_Int_89-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ULB_Int-89">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup> also becoming one of the largest convention centres in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-diplomatie_90-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-diplomatie-90">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup> The presence of the EU and the other international bodies has, for example, led to there being more ambassadors and journalists in Brussels than in <a href="/wiki/Washington,_D.C." title="Washington, D.C.">Washington D.C.</a><sup id="cite_ref-E!Sarp_91-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-E!Sarp-91">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup> International schools have also been established to serve this presence.<sup id="cite_ref-diplomatie_90-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-diplomatie-90">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup> The "international community" in Brussels numbers at least 70,000 people.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup> In 2009, there were an estimated 286 <a href="/wiki/Lobbying" title="Lobbying">lobbying</a> consultancies known to work in Brussels.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="European_Union">European Union</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brussels&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: European Union">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Brussels_and_the_European_Union" title="Brussels and the European Union">Brussels and the European Union</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Quartier_europ%C3%A9en_Bruxelles_2011-06_CROP.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Quartier_europ%C3%A9en_Bruxelles_2011-06_CROP.jpg/220px-Quartier_europ%C3%A9en_Bruxelles_2011-06_CROP.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="222" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Quartier_europ%C3%A9en_Bruxelles_2011-06_CROP.jpg/330px-Quartier_europ%C3%A9en_Bruxelles_2011-06_CROP.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Quartier_europ%C3%A9en_Bruxelles_2011-06_CROP.jpg/440px-Quartier_europ%C3%A9en_Bruxelles_2011-06_CROP.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1470" data-file-height="1482" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Quartier_europ%C3%A9en_Bruxelles_2011-06_CROP.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Aerial view of the <a href="/wiki/Brussels_and_the_European_Union#European_Quarter" title="Brussels and the European Union">European Quarter</a></div></div></div>\n<p>Brussels serves as <i><a href="/wiki/De_facto" title="De facto">de facto</a></i> capital of the European Union, hosting the major political <a href="/wiki/Institutions_of_the_European_Union" title="Institutions of the European Union">institutions of the Union</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Demey_23-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Demey-23">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> The EU has not declared a capital formally, though the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Amsterdam" title="Treaty of Amsterdam">Treaty of Amsterdam</a> formally gives Brussels the seat of the <a href="/wiki/European_Commission" title="European Commission">European Commission</a> (the executive branch of government) and the <a href="/wiki/Council_of_the_European_Union" title="Council of the European Union">Council of the European Union</a> (a legislative institution made up from executives of member states).<sup id="cite_ref-ENA_COMM_SEAT_94-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ENA_COMM_SEAT-94">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources#What_information_to_include" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="A complete citation is needed. (April 2018)">full citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup><sup id="cite_ref-EC_EiB_95-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EC_EiB-95">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources#What_information_to_include" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="A complete citation is needed. (April 2018)">full citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> It locates the formal seat of <a href="/wiki/European_Parliament" title="European Parliament">European Parliament</a> in <a href="/wiki/Strasbourg" title="Strasbourg">Strasbourg</a>, where votes take place, with the council, on the proposals made by the commission. However, meetings of political groups and committee groups are formally given to Brussels, along with a set number of plenary sessions. Three quarters of Parliament sessions now take place at its <a href="/wiki/Espace_L%C3%A9opold" title="Espace L\xc3\xa9opold">Brussels hemicycle</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup> Between 2002 and 2004, the <a href="/wiki/European_Council" title="European Council">European Council</a> also fixed its seat in the city.<sup id="cite_ref-Dragoman_97-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dragoman-97">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup> In 2014, the Union hosted a <a href="/wiki/40th_G7_summit" title="40th G7 summit">G7 summit</a> in the city.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_64-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-64">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:262px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Place_du_Luxembourg_889_Wide.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Place_du_Luxembourg_889_Wide.jpg/260px-Place_du_Luxembourg_889_Wide.jpg" decoding="async" width="260" height="129" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Place_du_Luxembourg_889_Wide.jpg/390px-Place_du_Luxembourg_889_Wide.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Place_du_Luxembourg_889_Wide.jpg/520px-Place_du_Luxembourg_889_Wide.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1924" data-file-height="953" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Place_du_Luxembourg_889_Wide.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Place_du_Luxembourg" title="Place du Luxembourg">Place du Luxembourg/Luxemburgplein</a> with the <a href="/wiki/European_Parliament" title="European Parliament">European Parliament</a> in the background</div></div></div>\n<p>Brussels, along with <a href="/wiki/Luxembourg_(city)" class="mw-redirect" title="Luxembourg (city)">Luxembourg</a> and Strasbourg, began to host European institutions in 1957, soon becoming the centre of activities, as the Commission and Council based their activities in what has become the <a href="/wiki/Brussels_and_the_European_Union" title="Brussels and the European Union"><i>European Quarter</i></a>, in the east of the city.<sup id="cite_ref-ENA_COMM_SEAT_94-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ENA_COMM_SEAT-94">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup> Early building in Brussels was sporadic and uncontrolled, with little planning. The current major buildings are the <a href="/wiki/Berlaymont_building" title="Berlaymont building">Berlaymont building</a> of the commission, symbolic of the quarter as a whole, the <a href="/wiki/Justus_Lipsius_building" title="Justus Lipsius building">Justus Lipsius building</a> of the Council and the <a href="/wiki/Espace_L%C3%A9opold" title="Espace L\xc3\xa9opold">Espace L\xc3\xa9opold</a> of the Parliament.<sup id="cite_ref-EC_EiB_95-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EC_EiB-95">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup> Today, the presence has increased considerably, with the Commission alone occupying 865,000&#160;m<sup>2</sup> (9,310,000&#160;sq&#160;ft) within the <i>European Quarter</i> (a quarter of the total office space in Brussels<sup id="cite_ref-Demey_23-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Demey-23">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>). The concentration and density has caused concern that the presence of the institutions has created a <i><a href="/wiki/Ghetto" title="Ghetto">ghetto</a> effect</i> in that part of the city.<sup id="cite_ref-EUO_buildings_98-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EUO_buildings-98">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup> However, the European presence has contributed significantly to the importance of Brussels as an international centre.<sup id="cite_ref-E!Sarp_91-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-E!Sarp-91">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<style data-file-height="510" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption text-align-center">The <a href="/wiki/Europa_building" title="Europa building">Europa building</a> (<b><a href="/wiki/European_Council" title="European Council">European Council</a></b>)</div></div><div class="tsingle" style="width:252px;max-width:252px"><div class="thumbimage"><a height="156" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Building_of_the_European_Parliament_in_Brussels.jpg/375px-Building_of_the_European_Parliament_in_Brussels.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Building_of_the_European_Parliament_in_Brussels.jpg/500px-Building_of_the_European_Parliament_in_Brussels.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1840" data-file-height="1150" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption text-align-center">The <a href="/wiki/Espace_L%C3%A9opold" title="Espace L\xc3\xa9opold">Espace L\xc3\xa9opold</a> buildings (<b><a href="/wiki/European_Parliament" title="European Parliament">European Parliament</a></b>)</div></div></div></div></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Eurocontrol">Eurocontrol</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brussels&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Eurocontrol">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Eurocontrol" title="Eurocontrol">Eurocontrol</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Eurocontrol_hoofdkwartier_1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Eurocontrol_hoofdkwartier_1.jpg/220px-Eurocontrol_hoofdkwartier_1.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Eurocontrol_hoofdkwartier_1.jpg/330px-Eurocontrol_hoofdkwartier_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Eurocontrol_hoofdkwartier_1.jpg/440px-Eurocontrol_hoofdkwartier_1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="400" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Eurocontrol_hoofdkwartier_1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Headquarters of <a href="/wiki/Eurocontrol" title="Eurocontrol">Eurocontrol</a> in <a href="/wiki/Haren,_Belgium" title="Haren, Belgium">Haren</a></div></div></div>\n<p>The European Organisation for the Safety of Air Navigation, commonly known as Eurocontrol, is an <a href="/wiki/International_organisation" class="mw-redirect" title="International organisation">international organisation</a> which coordinates and plans <a href="/wiki/Air_traffic_control" title="Air traffic control">air traffic control</a> across European <a href="/wiki/Airspace" title="Airspace">airspace</a>. The corporation was founded in 1960 and has 41 member states. Its headquarters are located in <a href="/wiki/Haren,_Belgium" title="Haren, Belgium">Haren</a>, on the northeast perimeter of the <a href="/wiki/City_of_Brussels" title="City of Brussels">City of Brussels</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="North_Atlantic_Treaty_Organisation">North Atlantic Treaty Organisation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brussels&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: North Atlantic Treaty Organisation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/NATO_headquarters" title="NATO headquarters">NATO headquarters</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:2018_NATO_Summit_in_Brussels_(29510554308).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/2018_NATO_Summit_in_Brussels_%2829510554308%29.jpg/220px-2018_NATO_Summit_in_Brussels_%2829510554308%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/2018_NATO_Summit_in_Brussels_%2829510554308%29.jpg/330px-2018_NATO_Summit_in_Brussels_%2829510554308%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/2018_NATO_Summit_in_Brussels_%2829510554308%29.jpg/440px-2018_NATO_Summit_in_Brussels_%2829510554308%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="6979" data-file-height="4653" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:2018_NATO_Summit_in_Brussels_(29510554308).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Flags of <a href="/wiki/Member_states_of_NATO" title="Member states of NATO">NATO member states</a> wave at the entrance of <a href="/wiki/NATO_Headquarters" class="mw-redirect" title="NATO Headquarters">NATO\'s headquarters</a> in <a href="/wiki/Haren,_Belgium" title="Haren, Belgium">Haren</a></div></div></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Brussels" title="Treaty of Brussels">Treaty of Brussels</a>, which was signed on 17 March 1948 between Belgium, <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a>, <a href="/wiki/Luxembourg" title="Luxembourg">Luxembourg</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Netherlands" title="Netherlands">Netherlands</a> and the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a>, was a prelude to the establishment of the <a href="/wiki/Intergovernmental_organization" title="Intergovernmental organization">intergovernmental</a> <a href="/wiki/Military_alliance" title="Military alliance">military alliance</a> which later became the North Atlantic Treaty Organization (NATO).<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup> Today, the alliance consists of 29 independent member countries across <a href="/wiki/North_America" title="North America">North America</a> and Europe. Several countries also have diplomatic missions to NATO <a href="/wiki/List_of_diplomatic_missions_to_NATO" class="mw-redirect" title="List of diplomatic missions to NATO">through embassies in Belgium</a>. Since 1949, a number of <a href="/wiki/NATO_summit" title="NATO summit">NATO Summits</a> have been held in Brussels,<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup> the most recent taking place in May 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup> The organisation\'s political and administrative <a href="/wiki/NATO_Headquarters" class="mw-redirect" title="NATO Headquarters">headquarters</a> are located on <span lang="fr" style="font-style: normal;" title="French-language text">Boulevard L\xc3\xa9opold III</span>/<span lang="nl" style="font-style: normal;" title="Dutch-language text">Leopold III-laan</span> in <a href="/wiki/Haren,_Belgium" title="Haren, Belgium">Haren</a>, Brussels.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup> A new \xe2\x82\xac750&#160;million headquarters building begun in 2010 and was completed in 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brussels&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Population">Population</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brussels&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Population">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:EU_NUTS_2_population_density_2007.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/EU_NUTS_2_population_density_2007.svg/220px-EU_NUTS_2_population_density_2007.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="155" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/EU_NUTS_2_population_density_2007.svg/330px-EU_NUTS_2_population_density_2007.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/EU_NUTS_2_population_density_2007.svg/440px-EU_NUTS_2_population_density_2007.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="850" data-file-height="600" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:EU_NUTS_2_population_density_2007.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Population_density" title="Population density">Population density</a> of Europe. Brussels is located between the largest urban centres.</div></div></div>\n<p>Brussels is located in one of the most <a href="/wiki/Blue_Banana" title="Blue Banana">urbanised regions of Europe</a>, between <a href="/wiki/Paris" title="Paris">Paris</a>, <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Rhine-Ruhr" title="Rhine-Ruhr">Rhine-Ruhr</a> (<a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">Germany</a>), and the <a href="/wiki/Randstad" title="Randstad">Randstad</a> (<a href="/wiki/Netherlands" title="Netherlands">Netherlands</a>). The Brussels-Capital Region has a population of around 1.2&#160;million and has witnessed, in recent years, a remarkable increase in its population. In general, the population of Brussels is younger than the national average, and the gap between rich and poor is wider.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Brussels is the core of a built-up area that extends well beyond the region\'s limits. Sometimes referred to as the urban area of Brussels (French: <i lang="fr">aire urbaine de Bruxelles</i>, Dutch: <i lang="nl">stedelijk gebied van Brussel</i>) or Greater Brussels (French: <i lang="fr">Grand-Bruxelles</i>, Dutch: <i lang="nl">Groot-Brussel</i>), this area extends over a large part of the two Brabant provinces, including much of the surrounding <a href="/wiki/Arrondissement_of_Halle-Vilvoorde" title="Arrondissement of Halle-Vilvoorde">arrondissement of Halle-Vilvoorde</a> and some small parts of the <a href="/wiki/Arrondissement_of_Leuven" title="Arrondissement of Leuven">arrondissement of Leuven</a> in <a href="/wiki/Flemish_Brabant" title="Flemish Brabant">Flemish Brabant</a>, as well as the northern part of <a href="/wiki/Walloon_Brabant" title="Walloon Brabant">Walloon Brabant</a>.\n</p><p>The metropolitan area of Brussels is divided into three levels. Firstly, the central agglomeration (within the regional borders), with a population of 1,218,255 inhabitants.<sup id="cite_ref-:8_17-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:8-17">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> Adding the closest suburbs (French: <i lang="fr">banlieues</i>, Dutch: <i lang="nl">buitenwijken</i>) gives a total population of 1,831,496. Including the outer <a href="/wiki/Commuter" class="mw-redirect" title="Commuter">commuter</a> zone (<a href="/wiki/Brussels_Regional_Express_Network" title="Brussels Regional Express Network">Brussels Regional Express Network</a> (RER/GEN) area), the population is 2,676,701.<sup id="cite_ref-BelMetr_19-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BelMetr-19">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:5_20-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:5-20">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> Brussels is also part of a wider <a href="/wiki/Flemish_Diamond" title="Flemish Diamond">diamond-shaped</a> <a href="/wiki/Conurbation" title="Conurbation">conurbation</a>, with <a href="/wiki/Ghent" title="Ghent">Ghent</a>, <a href="/wiki/Antwerp" title="Antwerp">Antwerp</a> and <a href="/wiki/Leuven" title="Leuven">Leuven</a>, which has about 4.4&#160;million inhabitants (a little more than 40% of the Belgium\'s total population).<sup id="cite_ref-:6_21-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:6-21">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Meijers-2007_105-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Meijers-2007-105">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable">\n<tbody><tr>\n<th><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability"><span title="The material near this tag needs to be fact-checked with the cited source(s). (February 2018)">verification needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</th>\n<th>01-07-2004<sup id="cite_ref-statbe12_106-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-statbe12-106">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup>\n</th>\n<th>01-07-2005<sup id="cite_ref-statbe12_106-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-statbe12-106">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup>\n</th>\n<th>01-07-2006<sup id="cite_ref-statbe12_106-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-statbe12-106">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup>\n</th>\n<th>01-01-2008<sup id="cite_ref-statbe12_106-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-statbe12-106">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup>\n</th>\n<th>01-01-2015<sup id="cite_ref-statbe12_106-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-statbe12-106">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup>\n</th>\n<th>01-01-2019<sup id="cite_ref-statbe12_106-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-statbe12-106">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup>\n</th>\n<th>01-01-2020<sup id="cite_ref-statbe12_106-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-statbe12-106">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup>\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><b>Brussels-Capital Region<sup id="cite_ref-statbe12_106-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-statbe12-106">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup></b><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability"><span title="The material near this tag needs to be fact-checked with the cited source(s). style="text-align:right;"><i>277.682</i>\n</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;"><i>295.043</i>\n</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;"><i>385.381</i>\n</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;"><i>450.000</i>\n</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;"><i>?</i>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Nationalities">Nationalities</span><span States</td>\n<td>3,137\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>Brussels is home to a large number of immigrants and people of immigrant background. At the last Belgian census in 1991, 63.7% of inhabitants in Brussels-Capital Region answered that they were Belgian citizens, born as such in Belgium.<sup id="cite_ref-philippevanparijs_108-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-philippevanparijs-108">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ibsa_109-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ibsa-109">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup> However, there have been numerous individual or familial migrations towards Brussels since the end of the 18th century, including <a href="/wiki/Right_of_asylum" title="Right of asylum">political refugees</a> (<a href="/wiki/Karl_Marx" title="Karl Marx">Karl Marx</a>, <a href="/wiki/Victor_Hugo" title="Victor Hugo">Victor Hugo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pierre-Joseph_Proudhon" title="Pierre-Joseph Proudhon">Pierre Joseph Proudhon</a>, <a href="/wiki/L%C3%A9on_Daudet" title="L\xc3\xa9on Daudet">L\xc3\xa9on Daudet</a>, for example), from neighbouring or more distant countries, as well as labour migrants, former foreign students or <a href="/wiki/Expatriate" title="Expatriate">expatriates</a>, and many Belgian families in Brussels can claim at least one foreign grandparent.\n</p><p>This large concentration of immigrants and their descendance includes many of Moroccan (mainly <a href="/wiki/Riffian_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Riffian people">Riffian</a> and <a href="/wiki/Berbers" title="Berbers">Berber</a>) and Turkish ancestry, together with French-speaking black Africans from former <a href="/wiki/Belgian_overseas_colonies" class="mw-redirect" title="Belgian overseas colonies">Belgian colonies</a>, such as the <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Democratic Republic of the Congo">Democratic Republic of the Congo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rwanda" title="Rwanda">Rwanda</a> and <a href="/wiki/Burundi" title="Burundi">Burundi</a>. People of foreign origin make up nearly 70%<sup id="cite_ref-philippevanparijs_108-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-philippevanparijs-108">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup> of the population of Brussels, most of whom have been <a href="/wiki/Naturalization" title="Naturalization">naturalised</a> following the great 1991 reform of the naturalisation process. About 32% of city residents are of non-Belgian <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">European</a> origin (mainly expatriates from France, Romania, Italy, Spain, Poland, and Portugal) and 36% are of another background, mostly from <a href="/wiki/Morocco" title="Morocco">Morocco</a>, <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkey</a> and Sub-Saharan <a href="/wiki/Africa" title="Africa">Africa</a>. Among all major migrant groups from outside the EU, a majority of the permanent residents have acquired Belgian nationality.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>According to Statbel, the Belgian statistical office, in 2020, taking into account the nationality of birth of the parents, 74.3% of the population of the Brussels-Capital region was of foreign origin and 41.8% was of non-European origin (including 28.7% of African origin). Among those aged under 18, 88% were of foreign origin and 57% of non-European origin (including 42.4% of African origin).<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">Languages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brussels&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Languages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Francization_of_Brussels" title="Francization of Brussels">Francization of Brussels</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Languages_spoken_at_home_in_the_Brussels_Capital_Region_(2013).PNG" class="image"><img alt="" decoding="async" width="220" height="192" class="thumbimage" 1.5x,
