2x" data-file-width="487" data-file-height="424" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Languages_spoken_at_home_in_the_Brussels_Capital_Region_(2013).PNG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Estimate of languages spoken at home (Capital Region, 2013)<sup id="cite_ref-brio2013_113-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-brio2013-113">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup><br /><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color" style="background-color:#9999FF; color:black;">&#160;</span>&#160;French</div><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color" style="background-color:#CCCCFF; color:black;">&#160;</span>&#160;Dutch and French</div><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color" style="background-color:#CCFFFF; color:black;">&#160;</span>&#160;Dutch</div><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color" style="background-color:#99CCFF; color:black;">&#160;</span>&#160;French and other language</div><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color" style="background-color:#FFFFCC; color:black;">&#160;</span>&#160;Neither Dutch nor French</div></div></div></div>\n<p>Historically a <a href="/wiki/Dutch_language" title="Dutch language">Dutch-speaking</a> city (<a href="/wiki/Brabantian_dialect" title="Brabantian dialect">Brabantian dialect</a> to be exact),<sup id="cite_ref-tokyo_114-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tokyo-114">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-jaumain_115-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jaumain-115">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-roegiest_116-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-roegiest-116">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup> over the two past centuries<sup id="cite_ref-tokyo_114-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tokyo-114">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-marynissen_117-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-marynissen-117">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a> (specifically <a href="/wiki/Belgian_French" title="Belgian French">Belgian French</a>) has become the majority language and <i><a href="/wiki/Lingua_franca" title="Lingua franca">lingua franca</a></i> in Brussels.<sup id="cite_ref-rudi3_118-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rudi3-118">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup> The main cause of this transition was the rapid <a href="/wiki/Cultural_assimilation" title="Cultural assimilation">assimilation</a> of the local <a href="/wiki/Flemish_people" title="Flemish people">Flemish population</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-kramer_119-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kramer-119">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-tokyo_114-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tokyo-114">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-baetens_120-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-baetens-120">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ernst_121-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ernst-121">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-roegiest_116-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-roegiest-116">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup> amplified by immigration from <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wallonia" title="Wallonia">Wallonia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-tokyo_114-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tokyo-114">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-vermeersch_122-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-vermeersch-122">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Francization" title="Francization">rise of French</a> in public life gradually began by the end of the 18th century,<sup id="cite_ref-poirier_123-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-poirier-123">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-rousseaux_124-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rousseaux-124">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup> quickly accelerating after <a href="/wiki/Belgian_Revolution" title="Belgian Revolution">Belgian independence</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-degroof_125-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-degroof-125">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-gubin_126-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gubin-126">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup> Dutch \xe2\x80\x94 of which <a href="/wiki/Standard_language" title="Standard language">standardisation</a> in Belgium was still very weak<sup id="cite_ref-balans_127-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-balans-127">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-busekist_128-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-busekist-128">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-gubin_126-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gubin-126">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup> \xe2\x80\x94 could not compete with French, which was the exclusive language of the judiciary, the administration, the army, education, cultural life and the media, and thus necessary for <a href="/wiki/Social_mobility" title="Social mobility">social mobility</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-bitsch_129-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bitsch-129">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-t\xc3\xa9tart_130-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-t\xc3\xa9tart-130">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-jaumain_115-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jaumain-115">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-kok_131-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kok-131">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-marynissen_117-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-marynissen-117">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup> The value and prestige of the French language was universally acknowledged<sup id="cite_ref-jaumain_115-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jaumain-115">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-bogaert_132-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bogaert-132">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-kramer_119-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kramer-119">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-gubin_126-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gubin-126">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-hasquin2_133-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hasquin2-133">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-vrints_134-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-vrints-134">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup> to such an extent that after 1880,<sup id="cite_ref-veron_135-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-veron-135">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-velthoven_136-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-velthoven-136">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-balans_127-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-balans-127">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup> and more particularly after the turn of the 20th century,<sup id="cite_ref-gubin_126-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gubin-126">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup> proficiency in French among Dutch-speakers in Brussels increased spectacularly.<sup id="cite_ref-blampain_137-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-blampain-137">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Although the majority of the population remained bilingual until the second half of the 20th century,<sup id="cite_ref-blampain_137-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-blampain-137">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-kramer_119-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kramer-119">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup> the original Brabantian dialect<sup id="cite_ref-witte_138-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-witte-138">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup> was often no longer passed down from one generation to another,<sup id="cite_ref-treffers_139-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-treffers-139">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup> leading to an increase of monolingual French-speakers from 1910 onwards.<sup id="cite_ref-bogaert_132-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bogaert-132">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-metsenaere-thuis_140-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-metsenaere-thuis-140">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup> From the mid-20th century, the number of monolingual French-speakers surpassed the number of mostly bilingual Flemish inhabitants.<sup id="cite_ref-brio4_141-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-brio4-141">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup> This process of assimilation weakened after the 1960s,<sup id="cite_ref-blampain_137-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-blampain-137">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-mares_142-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mares-142">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup> as the <a href="/wiki/Language_border" title="Language border">language border</a> was fixed, the status of Dutch as an official language of Belgium was reinforced,<sup id="cite_ref-depr\xc3\xa9_143-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-depr\xc3\xa9-143">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup> and the economic centre of gravity shifted northward to <a href="/wiki/Flanders" title="Flanders">Flanders</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-balans_127-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-balans-127">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-veron_135-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-veron-135">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup> However, with the continuing arrival of immigrants and the post-war emergence of Brussels as a <a href="/wiki/Brussels_and_the_European_Union" title="Brussels and the European Union">centre of international politics</a>, the relative position of Dutch continued to decline.<sup id="cite_ref-brusselsstudies_144-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-brusselsstudies-144">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-marynissen_117-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-marynissen-117">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-janssens_145-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-janssens-145">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-detant_146-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-detant-146">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-blampain_137-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-blampain-137">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-treffers_139-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-treffers-139">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup> Furthermore, as Brussels\' urban area expanded,<sup id="cite_ref-meynen_147-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-meynen-147">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup> a further number of Dutch-speaking municipalities in the <a href="/wiki/Brussels_Periphery" title="Brussels Periphery">Brussels periphery</a> also became predominantly French-speaking.<sup id="cite_ref-depr\xc3\xa9_143-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-depr\xc3\xa9-143">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-klinkenberg_148-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-klinkenberg-148">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup> This phenomenon of expanding Francisation \xe2\x80\x94 dubbed "oil slick" by its opponents<sup id="cite_ref-kramer_119-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kramer-119">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-kesteloot_149-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kesteloot-149">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-blampain_137-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-blampain-137">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup> \xe2\x80\x94 is, together with the future of Brussels,<sup id="cite_ref-frognier_150-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-frognier-150">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup> one of the most controversial topics in <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Belgium" title="Politics of Belgium">Belgian politics</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-veron_135-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-veron-135">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-t\xc3\xa9tart_130-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-t\xc3\xa9tart-130">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Brussels_signs.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Brussels_signs.jpg/220px-Brussels_signs.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Brussels_signs.jpg/330px-Brussels_signs.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Brussels_signs.jpg/440px-Brussels_signs.jpg 2x" data-file-width="552" data-file-height="368" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Brussels_signs.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Bilingual French and Dutch street signs in Brussels</div></div></div>\n<p>Today, the Brussels-Capital Region is officially bilingual in French and Dutch,<sup id="cite_ref-constitution_151-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-constitution-151">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup> as is the administration of the 19 municipalities.<sup id="cite_ref-brusselsstudies_144-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-brusselsstudies-144">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup> The creation of this bilingual, full-fledged region, with its own competencies and jurisdiction, had long been hampered by different visions of Belgian federalism. Nevertheless, some communitarian issues remain.<sup id="cite_ref-jacobs_152-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jacobs-152">&#91;149&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-debruycker_153-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-debruycker-153">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup> Flemish political parties demanded, for decades, that the Flemish part of <a href="/wiki/Brussels-Halle-Vilvoorde" title="Brussels-Halle-Vilvoorde">Brussels-Halle-Vilvoorde</a> (BHV) <i>arrondissement</i> be separated from the Brussels Region (which made Halle-Vilvoorde a monolingual Flemish electoral and judicial district). BHV was divided mid-2012. The French-speaking population regards the language border as artificial<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup> and demands the extension of the bilingual region to at least all six <a href="/wiki/Municipalities_with_language_facilities" title="Municipalities with language facilities">municipalities with language facilities</a> in the surroundings of Brussels.<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">&#91;d&#93;</a></sup> Flemish politicians have strongly rejected these proposals.<sup id="cite_ref-question_156-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-question-156">&#91;152&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">&#91;153&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Arrondissement_Brussels-Periphery_Belgium_Map.PNG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Arrondissement_Brussels-Periphery_Belgium_Map.PNG/220px-Arrondissement_Brussels-Periphery_Belgium_Map.PNG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/0/0f/Arrondissement_Brussels-Periphery_Belgium_Map.PNG 1.5x" data-file-width="270" data-file-height="203" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Arrondissement_Brussels-Periphery_Belgium_Map.PNG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Municipalities_with_language_facilities" title="Municipalities with language facilities">municipalities with language facilities</a> (in red) near Brussels</div></div></div>\n<p>Besides, owing to migration and to its international role, Brussels is home to a growing number of foreign language speakers. Currently, the first language of roughly half of the inhabitants is not an official one of the Capital Region.<sup id="cite_ref-standaard_159-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-standaard-159">&#91;155&#93;</a></sup> In 2013, academic research showed that approximately 17% of families spoke none of the official languages in the home, while in a further 23% a foreign language was used alongside French. The share of unilingual French-speaking families had fallen to 38% and that of Dutch-speaking families to 5%, while the percentage of bilingual Dutch-French families reached 17%. In 2013, French was spoken "well to perfectly" by 88% of the population and Dutch by 23% (down from 33% in 2000),<sup id="cite_ref-brusselsstudies_144-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-brusselsstudies-144">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup> while the other most commonly known languages were English at 30%, Arabic at 18%, Spanish at 9%, German at 7% and Italian and Turkish at around 5%.<sup id="cite_ref-brio2013_113-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-brio2013-113">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup> Despite the rise of English as a second language in Brussels, including as an unofficial compromise language between French and Dutch, as well as the working language for some of its international businesses and institutions, French remains the <i>lingua franca</i> and all public services are conducted exclusively in French or Dutch.<sup id="cite_ref-brusselsstudies_144-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-brusselsstudies-144">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The original dialect of Brussels (known as <i>Brussels</i>, and also sometimes called <a href="/wiki/Marols" title="Marols">Marols</a> or Marollien),<sup id="cite_ref-Jeanine_Treffers-Daller_1994_46-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Jeanine_Treffers-Daller_1994-46">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> a form of <a href="/wiki/Brabantic" class="mw-redirect" title="Brabantic">Brabantic</a> (the variant of Dutch spoken in the ancient <a href="/wiki/Duchy_of_Brabant" title="Duchy of Brabant">Duchy of Brabant</a>) with a significant number of loanwords from French, still survives among a small minority of inhabitants called <i>Brusseleers</i><sup id="cite_ref-evans_47-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-evans-47">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> (or <i>Brusseleirs</i>), many of them quite bi- and multilingual, or educated in French and not writing in Dutch.<sup id="cite_ref-winkler_160-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-winkler-160">&#91;156&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Jeanine_Treffers-Daller_1994_46-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Jeanine_Treffers-Daller_1994-46">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> The ethnic and national self-identification of Brussels\' inhabitants is nonetheless sometimes quite distinct from the French and Dutch-speaking communities. For the French-speakers, it can vary from Francophone Belgian, <i lang="fr" title="French-language text">Bruxellois</i><sup id="cite_ref-Lerond,_1980_pp._477_49-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lerond,_1980_pp._477-49">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> (French <a href="/wiki/Demonym" title="Demonym">demonym</a> for an inhabitant of Brussels), <a href="/wiki/Walloons" title="Walloons">Walloon</a> (for people who migrated from the Walloon Region at an adult age); for Flemings living in Brussels, it is mainly either Dutch-speaking Belgian, Flemish or <i lang="nl" title="Dutch-language text">Brusselaar</i> (Dutch demonym for an inhabitant), and often both. For the <i>Brusseleers</i>, many simply consider themselves as belonging to Brussels.<sup id="cite_ref-Jeanine_Treffers-Daller_1994_46-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Jeanine_Treffers-Daller_1994-46">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religions">Religions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brussels&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Religions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Belgium" title="Religion in Belgium">Religion in Belgium</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bruxelles-Koekelberg,_kathedraal_foto4_2011-09-23_17.15.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Bruxelles-Koekelberg%2C_kathedraal_foto4_2011-09-23_17.15.JPG/220px-Bruxelles-Koekelberg%2C_kathedraal_foto4_2011-09-23_17.15.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Bruxelles-Koekelberg%2C_kathedraal_foto4_2011-09-23_17.15.JPG/330px-Bruxelles-Koekelberg%2C_kathedraal_foto4_2011-09-23_17.15.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Bruxelles-Koekelberg%2C_kathedraal_foto4_2011-09-23_17.15.JPG/440px-Bruxelles-Koekelberg%2C_kathedraal_foto4_2011-09-23_17.15.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3456" data-file-height="2592" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bruxelles-Koekelberg,_kathedraal_foto4_2011-09-23_17.15.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Basilica_of_the_Sacred_Heart,_Brussels" title="Basilica of the Sacred Heart, Brussels">National Basilica of the Sacred Heart</a> in <a href="/wiki/Koekelberg" title="Koekelberg">Koekelberg</a></div></div></div>\n<p>Historically, Brussels has been predominantly <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">Roman Catholic</a>, especially since the expulsion of <a href="/wiki/Protestantism" title="Protestantism">Protestants</a> in the 16th century. This is clear from the large number of historical churches in the region, particularly in the <a href="/wiki/City_of_Brussels" title="City of Brussels">City of Brussels</a>. The pre-eminent Catholic <a href="/wiki/Cathedral" title="Cathedral">cathedral</a> in Brussels is the <a href="/wiki/Cathedral_of_St._Michael_and_St._Gudula" title="Cathedral of St. Michael and St. Gudula">Cathedral of St. Michael and St. Gudula</a>, serving as the <a href="/wiki/Co-cathedral" title="Co-cathedral">co-cathedral</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Archdiocese_of_Mechelen-Brussels" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman Catholic Archdiocese of Mechelen-Brussels">Archdiocese of Mechelen\xe2\x80\x93Brussels</a>. On the northwestern side of the region, the <a href="/wiki/Basilica_of_the_Sacred_Heart,_Brussels" title="Basilica of the Sacred Heart, Brussels">National Basilica of the Sacred Heart</a> is a Minor Basilica and parish church and the <a href="/wiki/List_of_largest_church_buildings" title="List of largest church buildings">14th largest church building</a> in the world. The <a href="/wiki/Church_of_Our_Lady_of_Laeken" title="Church of Our Lady of Laeken">Church of Our Lady of Laeken</a> holds the tombs of many members of the <a href="/wiki/Monarchy_of_Belgium" title="Monarchy of Belgium">Belgian royal family</a>, including all the former <a href="/wiki/List_of_Belgian_monarchs" title="List of Belgian monarchs">Belgian monarchs</a>, within the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Crypt_(Belgium)" title="Royal Crypt (Belgium)">Royal Crypt</a>.\n</p>\n<div class="PieChartTemplate thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px">\n<div style="background-color:white;margin:auto;position:relative;width:200px;height:200px;overflow:hidden;border-radius:100px;border:1px solid black">\n<div style="border:solid transparent;position:absolute;width:100px;line-height:0;left:0; top:0; border-width:0 200px 200px 0; border-color:Gray"></div><div style="border:solid transparent;position:absolute;width:100px;line-height:0;right:100px; top:100px; border-width:95.105651629515px 30.901699437495px 0 0; border-top-color:yellow"></div>\n<div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 200px 100px 0;border-color:yellow"></div><div style="border:solid transparent;position:absolute;width:100px;line-height:0;right:100px; top:100px; border-width:84.432792550202px 53.5826794979px 0 0; border-top-color:dodgerblue"></div>\n<div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 200px 100px 0;border-color:dodgerblue"></div><div style="border:solid transparent;position:absolute;width:100px;line-height:0;right:100px; top:100px; border-width:72.896862742141px 68.454710592869px 0 0; border-top-color:Green"></div>\n<div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 200px 100px 0;border-color:Green"></div><div style="border:solid transparent;position:absolute;width:100px;line-height:0;right:100px; top:0; border-width:0 137.63819204712px 100px 0; border-right-color:Blue"></div>\n<div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;right:0;top:0;border-width:0 100px 100px 0;border-color:Blue"></div>\n</div>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<p>Religion in Brussels-Capital Region (2016)<sup id="cite_ref-2016religion_161-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2016religion-161">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color" style="background-color:Blue; color:white;">&#160;</span>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholicism" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman Catholicism">Roman Catholicism</a> (40%)</div><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color" style="background-color:Green; color:white;">&#160;</span>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a> (23%)</div><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color" style="background-color:dodgerblue; color:black;">&#160;</span>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Protestantism" title="Protestantism">Protestantism</a> (3%)</div><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color" style="background-color:yellow; color:black;">&#160;</span>&#160;Other religions (4%)</div><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color" style="background-color:Gray; color:black;">&#160;</span>&#160;Non-religious (30%)</div>\n</div>\n</div></div>\n<p>In reflection of its multicultural makeup, Brussels hosts a variety of religious communities, as well as large numbers of <a href="/wiki/Atheism" title="Atheism">atheists</a> and <a href="/wiki/Agnosticism" title="Agnosticism">agnostics</a>. Minority faiths include <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a>, <a href="/wiki/Anglicanism" title="Anglicanism">Anglicanism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Orthodox_Church" title="Eastern Orthodox Church">Eastern Orthodoxy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Judaism" title="Judaism">Judaism</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Buddhism" title="Buddhism">Buddhism</a>. According to a 2016 survey, approximately 40% of residents of Brussels declared themselves <a href="/wiki/Catholics" class="mw-redirect" title="Catholics">Catholics</a> (12% were practising Catholics and 28% were non-practising Catholics), 30% were <a href="/wiki/Irreligion" title="Irreligion">non-religious</a>, 23% were <a href="/wiki/Muslim" class="mw-redirect" title="Muslim">Muslim</a> (19% practising, 4% non-practising), 3% were <a href="/wiki/Protestant_Christian" class="mw-redirect" title="Protestant Christian">Protestants</a> and 4% were of another religion.<sup id="cite_ref-2016religion_161-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2016religion-161">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Recognised religions and <a href="/wiki/Secularism_in_Belgium" class="mw-redirect" title="Secularism in Belgium">laicism</a> enjoy public funding and school courses. It was once the case that every pupil in an official school from 6 years old to 18 had to choose 2 hours per week of compulsory religion\xe2\x80\x94or laicist\xe2\x80\x94inspired morals. However, in 2015, the Belgian Constitutional court ruled religious studies could no longer be required in the primary and secondary education system.<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Brussel_052_Jubelpark.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Brussel_052_Jubelpark.JPG/220px-Brussel_052_Jubelpark.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Brussel_052_Jubelpark.JPG/330px-Brussel_052_Jubelpark.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Brussel_052_Jubelpark.JPG/440px-Brussel_052_Jubelpark.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="2448" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Brussel_052_Jubelpark.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Great_Mosque_of_Brussels" title="Great Mosque of Brussels">Great Mosque of Brussels</a> is the seat of the Islamic and Cultural Centre of Belgium.</div></div></div>\n<p>Brussels has a large concentration of <a href="/wiki/Islam_in_Belgium" title="Islam in Belgium">Muslims</a>, mostly of Moroccan, Turkish, Syrian and Guinean ancestry. The <a href="/wiki/Great_Mosque_of_Brussels" title="Great Mosque of Brussels">Great Mosque of Brussels</a>, located in the <a href="/wiki/Cinquantenaire" title="Cinquantenaire">Parc du Cinquantenaire/Jubelpark</a>, is the oldest <a href="/wiki/Mosque" title="Mosque">mosque</a> in Brussels. Belgium does not collect statistics by ethnic background, so exact figures are unknown. It was estimated that, in 2005, people of Muslim background living in the Brussels Region numbered 256,220 and accounted for 25.5% of the city\'s population, a much higher concentration than those of the other regions of Belgium.<sup id="cite_ref-BuG_100_163-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BuG_100-163">&#91;159&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable">\n\n<tbody><tr>\n<th>Regions of Belgium<sup id="cite_ref-BuG_100_163-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BuG_100-163">&#91;159&#93;</a></sup> (1 January 2016)</th>\n<th>Total population</th>\n<th>People of Muslim origin</th>\n<th>% of Muslims\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>Belgium</td>\n<td>11,371,928</td>\n<td>603,642</td>\n<td>5.3%\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><b>Brussels-Capital Region</b></td>\n<td><b>1,180,531</b></td>\n<td><b>212,495</b></td>\n<td><b>18%</b>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><i>Wallonia</i></td>\n<td><i>3,395,942</i></td>\n<td><i>149,421</i></td>\n<td><i>4.4%</i>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><i>Flanders</i></td>\n<td><i>6,043,161</i></td>\n<td><i>241,726</i></td>\n<td><i>4.0%</i>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brussels&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Belgium" title="Culture of Belgium">Culture of Belgium</a></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Architecture">Architecture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brussels&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Architecture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The architecture in Brussels is diverse, and spans from the clashing combination of <a href="/wiki/Gothic_architecture" title="Gothic architecture">Gothic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Baroque_architecture" title="Baroque architecture">Baroque</a>, and <a href="/wiki/French_Baroque_architecture" title="French Baroque architecture">Louis XIV</a> styles on the <a href="/wiki/Grand_Place" title="Grand Place">Grand Place</a> to the <a href="/wiki/Postmodern_architecture" title="Postmodern architecture">postmodern</a> buildings of the <a href="/wiki/Brussels_and_the_European_Union" title="Brussels and the European Union">EU institutions</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">&#91;160&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bruxelles_Manneken_Pis.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Bruxelles_Manneken_Pis.jpg/170px-Bruxelles_Manneken_Pis.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="257" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Bruxelles_Manneken_Pis.jpg/255px-Bruxelles_Manneken_Pis.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Bruxelles_Manneken_Pis.jpg/340px-Bruxelles_Manneken_Pis.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2791" data-file-height="4216" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bruxelles_Manneken_Pis.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><i><a href="/wiki/Manneken_Pis" title="Manneken Pis">Manneken Pis</a></i> is a well-known public sculpture in Brussels.</div></div></div>\n<p>Very little <a href="/wiki/Medieval_architecture" title="Medieval architecture">medieval architecture</a> is preserved in Brussels. Buildings from that period are mostly found in the historic centre (called <i lang="fr" title="French-language text">\xc3\x8elot Sacr\xc3\xa9</i>), <a href="/wiki/Saint-G%C3%A9ry_Island" title="Saint-G\xc3\xa9ry Island"><i>Saint G\xc3\xa9ry</i>/<i>Sint-Goriks</i></a> and <i lang="fr" title="French-language text">Sainte-Catherine</i>/<i lang="nl" title="Dutch-language text">Sint Katelijne</i> neighbourhoods. The <a href="/wiki/Brabantine_Gothic" title="Brabantine Gothic">Brabantine Gothic</a> <a href="/wiki/Cathedral_of_St._Michael_and_St._Gudula" title="Cathedral of St. Michael and St. Gudula">Cathedral of St. Michael and St. Gudula</a> remains a prominent feature in the skyline of downtown Brussels. Isolated portions of the <a href="/wiki/First_walls_of_Brussels" class="mw-redirect" title="First walls of Brussels">first city walls</a> were saved from destruction and can be seen to this day. One of the only remains of the <a href="/wiki/Second_walls_of_Brussels" class="mw-redirect" title="Second walls of Brussels">second walls</a> is the <a href="/wiki/Halle_Gate" title="Halle Gate">Halle Gate</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Grand_Place" title="Grand Place">Grand Place</a> is the main attraction in the city centre and has been a <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Site" title="World Heritage Site">UNESCO World Heritage Site</a> since 1998.<sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">&#91;161&#93;</a></sup> The square is dominated by the 15th century <a href="/wiki/Flamboyant" title="Flamboyant">Flamboyant</a> <a href="/wiki/Brussels_Town_Hall" title="Brussels Town Hall">Town Hall</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Gothic_Revival_architecture" title="Gothic Revival architecture">neo-Gothic</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Museum_of_the_City_of_Brussels" class="mw-redirect" title="Museum of the City of Brussels">Breadhouse</a></i> and the Baroque <a href="/wiki/Guildhall" title="Guildhall">guildhalls</a> of the former <a href="/wiki/Guilds_of_Brussels" title="Guilds of Brussels">Guilds of Brussels</a>. <i><a href="/wiki/Manneken_Pis" title="Manneken Pis">Manneken Pis</a></i>, a fountain containing a small bronze sculpture of a urinating youth, is a tourist attraction and <a href="/wiki/Symbol" title="Symbol">symbol</a> of the city.<sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">&#91;162&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="center"><div class="thumb tnone"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:612px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Parterre_de_fleurs_Grand-place_de_Bruxelles_2016.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Parterre_de_fleurs_Grand-place_de_Bruxelles_2016.jpg/610px-Parterre_de_fleurs_Grand-place_de_Bruxelles_2016.jpg" decoding="async" width="610" height="182" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Parterre_de_fleurs_Grand-place_de_Bruxelles_2016.jpg/915px-Parterre_de_fleurs_Grand-place_de_Bruxelles_2016.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Parterre_de_fleurs_Grand-place_de_Bruxelles_2016.jpg/1220px-Parterre_de_fleurs_Grand-place_de_Bruxelles_2016.jpg 2x" data-file-width="22325" data-file-height="6643" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Parterre_de_fleurs_Grand-place_de_Bruxelles_2016.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Grand_Place" title="Grand Place">Grand Place of Brussels</a>, a <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a> <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Site" title="World Heritage Site">World Heritage Site</a></div></div></div></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Neoclassical_architecture" title="Neoclassical architecture">neoclassical</a> style of the 18th and 19th centuries is represented in the <i>Royal Quarter</i>/<i>Coudenberg</i> area, around <a href="/wiki/Brussels_Park" class="mw-redirect" title="Brussels Park">Brussels\' Park</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Place_Royale_(Brussels)" class="mw-redirect" title="Place Royale (Brussels)">Royal Square</a>. Examples include the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Palace_of_Brussels" title="Royal Palace of Brussels">Royal Palace</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Church_of_Saint_Jacques-sur-Coudenberg" class="mw-redirect" title="Church of Saint Jacques-sur-Coudenberg">Church of St. James on Coudenberg</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Belgian_Federal_Parliament" title="Belgian Federal Parliament">Palace of the Nation</a> (Parliament building), the <a href="/wiki/Academy_Palace" title="Academy Palace">Academy Palace</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Palace_of_Charles_of_Lorraine" title="Palace of Charles of Lorraine">Palace of Charles of Lorraine</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Palace_of_the_Count_of_Flanders" title="Palace of the Count of Flanders">Palace of the Count of Flanders</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Egmont_Palace" title="Egmont Palace">Egmont Palace</a>. Other uniform neoclassical ensembles can be found around <a href="/wiki/Place_des_Martyrs,_Brussels" title="Place des Martyrs, Brussels">Martyrs\' Square</a> and Barricades\' Square. Some additional landmarks in the centre are the <a href="/wiki/Galeries_Royales_Saint-Hubert" title="Galeries Royales Saint-Hubert">Royal Saint-Hubert Galleries</a> (1847), one of the oldest covered shopping arcades in Europe, the <a href="/wiki/Congress_Column" title="Congress Column">Congress Column</a> (1859), the former <a href="/wiki/Brussels_Stock_Exchange" title="Brussels Stock Exchange">Brussels Stock Exchange</a> building (1873) and the <a href="/wiki/Law_Courts_of_Brussels" class="mw-redirect" title="Law Courts of Brussels">Palace of Justice</a> (1883), designed by <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Poelaert" title="Joseph Poelaert">Joseph Poelaert</a>, in <a href="/wiki/Eclecticism_in_architecture" title="Eclecticism in architecture">eclectic</a> style, and reputed to be the largest building constructed in the 19th century.<sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">&#91;163&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Located outside the centre, in a greener environment, are the <a href="/wiki/Cinquantenaire" title="Cinquantenaire">Parc du Cinquantenaire/Jubelpark</a> with its <a href="/wiki/Arcade_du_Cinquantenaire" title="Arcade du Cinquantenaire">memorial arcade</a> and nearby museums, and in <a href="/wiki/Laeken" title="Laeken">Laeken</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Castle_of_Laeken" class="mw-redirect" title="Royal Castle of Laeken">Royal Castle of Laeken</a> and the Royal Domain with its large <a href="/wiki/Royal_Greenhouses_of_Laeken" title="Royal Greenhouses of Laeken">greenhouses</a>, as well as the <a href="/wiki/Museums_of_the_Far_East" title="Museums of the Far East">Museums of the Far East</a>.\n</p><p>Also particularly striking are the buildings in the <a href="/wiki/Art_Nouveau_in_Brussels" title="Art Nouveau in Brussels">Art Nouveau</a> style, most famously by the Belgian architects <a href="/wiki/Victor_Horta" title="Victor Horta">Victor Horta</a>, <a href="/wiki/Paul_Hankar" title="Paul Hankar">Paul Hankar</a> and <a href="/wiki/Henry_Van_de_Velde" class="mw-redirect" title="Henry Van de Velde">Henry Van de Velde</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">&#91;164&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">&#91;165&#93;</a></sup> Some of Brussels\' municipalities, such as <a href="/wiki/Schaerbeek" title="Schaerbeek">Schaerbeek</a>, <a href="/wiki/Etterbeek" title="Etterbeek">Etterbeek</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ixelles" title="Ixelles">Ixelles</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Saint-Gilles,_Belgium" title="Saint-Gilles, Belgium">Saint-Gilles</a>, were developed during the heyday of Art Nouveau and have many buildings in that style. The <a href="/wiki/Major_Town_Houses_of_the_Architect_Victor_Horta_(Brussels)" class="mw-redirect" title="Major Town Houses of the Architect Victor Horta (Brussels)">Major Town Houses of the Architect Victor Horta</a>\xe2\x80\x94<a href="/wiki/H%C3%B4tel_Tassel" title="H\xc3\xb4tel Tassel">H\xc3\xb4tel Tassel</a> (1893), <a href="/wiki/H%C3%B4tel_Solvay" title="H\xc3\xb4tel Solvay">H\xc3\xb4tel Solvay</a> (1894), <a href="/wiki/H%C3%B4tel_van_Eetvelde" title="H\xc3\xb4tel van Eetvelde">H\xc3\xb4tel van Eetvelde</a> (1895) and the <a href="/wiki/Horta_Museum" title="Horta Museum">Horta Museum</a> (1901)\xe2\x80\x94have been listed as a <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a> <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Site" title="World Heritage Site">World Heritage Site</a> since 2000.<sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170">&#91;166&#93;</a></sup> Another example of Brussels\' Art Nouveau is the <a href="/wiki/Stoclet_Palace" title="Stoclet Palace">Stoclet Palace</a> (1911), by the Viennese architect <a href="/wiki/Josef_Hoffmann" title="Josef Hoffmann">Josef Hoffmann</a>, designated a World Heritage Site by UNESCO in June 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171">&#91;167&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<ul class="gallery mw-gallery-packed">\n\t<li class="gallerycaption"><a href="/wiki/Art_Nouveau_in_Brussels" title="Art Nouveau in Brussels">Art Nouveau in Brussels</a></li>\n\t\t<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 103.33333333333px"><div style="width: 103.33333333333px">\n\t\t\t<div class="thumb" (1893)\n</p>\n\t\t\t</div>\n\t\t</div></li>\n\t\t<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 162px"><div style="width: 162px">\n\t\t\t<div class="thumb" style="width: 160px;"><div style="margin:0px auto;"><a decoding="async" width="160" height="160" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Tassel_House_stairway-00.JPG/360px-Tassel_House_stairway-00.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Tassel_House_stairway-00.JPG/480px-Tassel_House_stairway-00.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1440" data-file-height="1440" /></a></div></div>\n\t\t\t<div class="gallerytext">\n<p>Stairway in H\xc3\xb4tel Tassel\n</p>\n\t\t\t</div>\n\t\t</div></li>\n\t\t<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 112px"><div style="width: 112px">\n\t\t\t<div class="thumb" style="width: 110px;"><div style="margin:0px auto;"><a href="/wiki/File:H%C3%B4tel_Ciamberlani_(DSCF7523).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/H%C3%B4tel_Ciamberlani_%28DSCF7523%29.jpg/165px-H%C3%B4tel_Ciamberlani_%28DSCF7523%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="110" height="160" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/H%C3%B4tel_Ciamberlani_%28DSCF7523%29.jpg/248px-H%C3%B4tel_Ciamberlani_%28DSCF7523%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/H%C3%B4tel_Ciamberlani_%28DSCF7523%29.jpg/331px-H%C3%B4tel_Ciamberlani_%28DSCF7523%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2644" data-file-height="3836" /></a></div></div>\n\t\t\t<div class="gallerytext">\n<p>H\xc3\xb4tel Ciamberlani by <a href="/wiki/Paul_Hankar" title="Paul Hankar">Paul Hankar</a> (1897)\n</p>\n\t\t\t</div>\n\t\t</div></li>\n\t\t<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 89.333333333333px"><div style="width: 89.333333333333px">\n\t\t\t<div class="thumb" style="width: 87.333333333333px;"><div style="margin:0px auto;"><a data-file-height="4480" /></a></div></div>\n\t\t\t<div class="gallerytext">\n<p>Former <a href="/wiki/Old_England_(department_store)" title="Old England (department store)">Old England</a> department store by <a href="/wiki/Paul_Saintenoy" title="Paul Saintenoy">Paul Saintenoy</a> (1899)\n</p>\n\t\t\t</div>\n\t\t</div></li>\n\t\t<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 101.33333333333px"><div style="width: 101.33333333333px">\n\t\t\t<div class="thumb" style="width: 99.333333333333px;"><div style="margin:0px auto;"><a href="/wiki/File:Maison_Saint-Cyr_(DSCF7558).jpg" class="image"><img /></a></div></div>\n\t\t\t<div class="gallerytext">\n<p>Saint-Cyr House by <a href="/wiki/Gustave_Strauven" title="Gustave Strauven">Gustave Strauven</a> (1903)\n</p>\n\t\t\t</div>\n\t\t</div></li>\n\t\t<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 73.333333333333px"><div style="width: 73.333333333333px">\n\t\t\t<div class="thumb" style="width: 71.333333333333px;"><div style="margin:0px auto;"><a href="/wiki/File:Maison_Cauchie-445.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/Maison_Cauchie-445.jpg/107px-Maison_Cauchie-445.jpg" decoding="async" width="72" height="160" //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/Maison_Cauchie-445.jpg/213px-Maison_Cauchie-445.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1780" data-file-height="4000" /></a></div></div>\n\t\t\t<div class="gallerytext">\n<p><a href="/wiki/Cauchie_House" title="Cauchie House">Cauchie House</a> by <a href="/w/index.php?title=Paul_Cauchie&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Paul Cauchie (page does not exist)">Paul Cauchie</a> (1905)\n</p>\n\t\t\t</div>\n\t\t</div></li>\n\t\t<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 162px"><div style="width: 162px">\n\t\t\t<div class="thumb" style="width: 160px;"><div style="margin:0px auto;"><a href="/wiki/File:Maison_Cauchie_sgraffitopaneel.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Maison_Cauchie_sgraffitopaneel.jpg/240px-Maison_Cauchie_sgraffitopaneel.jpg" decoding="async" width="160" height="160" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Maison_Cauchie_sgraffitopaneel.jpg/360px-Maison_Cauchie_sgraffitopaneel.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Maison_Cauchie_sgraffitopaneel.jpg/480px-Maison_Cauchie_sgraffitopaneel.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2798" data-file-height="2798" /></a></div></div>\n\t\t\t<div class="gallerytext">\n<p><a href="/wiki/Sgraffito" title="Sgraffito">Sgraffito</a> panel in Cauchie House\n</p>\n\t\t\t</div>\n\t\t</div></li>\n\t\t<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 286.66666666667px"><div style="width: 286.66666666667px">\n\t\t\t<div class="thumb" style="width: 284.66666666667px;"><div style="margin:0px auto;"><a href="/wiki/File:20120923_Brussels_PalaisStoclet_Hoffmann_DSC06725_PtrQs.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/20120923_Brussels_PalaisStoclet_Hoffmann_DSC06725_PtrQs.jpg/427px-20120923_Brussels_PalaisStoclet_Hoffmann_DSC06725_PtrQs.jpg" decoding="async" width="285" height="160" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/20120923_Brussels_PalaisStoclet_Hoffmann_DSC06725_PtrQs.jpg/640px-20120923_Brussels_PalaisStoclet_Hoffmann_DSC06725_PtrQs.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/20120923_Brussels_PalaisStoclet_Hoffmann_DSC06725_PtrQs.jpg/854px-20120923_Brussels_PalaisStoclet_Hoffmann_DSC06725_PtrQs.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5276" data-file-height="2968" /></a></div></div>\n\t\t\t<div class="gallerytext">\n<p><a href="/wiki/Stoclet_Palace" title="Stoclet Palace">Stoclet Palace</a> by <a href="/wiki/Josef_Hoffmann" title="Josef Hoffmann">Josef Hoffmann</a> (1911)\n</p>\n\t\t\t</div>\n\t\t</div></li>\n</ul>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Art_Deco_in_Brussels" title="Art Deco in Brussels">Art Deco</a> structures in Brussels include the Residence Palace (1927) (now part of the <a href="/wiki/Europa_building" title="Europa building">Europa building</a>), the <a href="/wiki/Centre_for_Fine_Arts,_Brussels" title="Centre for Fine Arts, Brussels">Centre for Fine Arts</a> (1928), the <a href="/wiki/Villa_Empain" title="Villa Empain">Villa Empain</a> (1934), the <a href="/wiki/Forest_Town_Hall" title="Forest Town Hall">Town Hall of Forest</a> (1938), and the <a href="/wiki/Le_Flagey" title="Le Flagey">Flagey Building</a> (formerly known as the <i>Maison de la Radio</i>) on <a href="/wiki/Place_Flagey" title="Place Flagey">Eug\xc3\xa8ne Flagey Square</a> (1938) in Ixelles. Some religious buildings from the <a href="/wiki/Interwar_period" title="Interwar period">interwar era</a> were also constructed in that style, such as the <a href="/wiki/Church_of_St._John_the_Baptist,_Molenbeek" title="Church of St. John the Baptist, Molenbeek">Church of St. John the Baptist</a> (1932) in Molenbeek and the <a href="/wiki/Church_of_St._Augustine,_Forest" title="Church of St. Augustine, Forest">Church of St. Augustine</a> (1935) in Forest. Completed only in 1969, and combining Art Deco with <a href="/wiki/Byzantine_Revival_architecture" title="Byzantine Revival architecture">neo-Byzantine</a> elements, the <a href="/wiki/Basilica_of_the_Sacred_Heart,_Brussels" title="Basilica of the Sacred Heart, Brussels">Basilica of the Sacred Heart</a> in <a href="/wiki/Koekelberg" title="Koekelberg">Koekelberg</a> is one of the <a href="/wiki/List_of_largest_church_buildings" title="List of largest church buildings">largest</a> <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">Roman Catholic</a> basilicas by area in the world, and its cupola provides a panoramic view of Brussels and its outskirts. Another example are the exhibition halls of the Centenary Palace, built for the <a href="/wiki/Brussels_International_Exposition_(1935)" title="Brussels International Exposition (1935)">1935 World\'s Fair</a> on the <a href="/wiki/Heysel_Plateau" title="Heysel Plateau"><i>Heysel</i>/<i>Heizel</i> Plateau</a> in northern Brussels, and home to the Brussels Exhibition Centre (Brussels Expo).<sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">&#91;168&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ancien_Institut_national_de_Radiodiffusion_-_vue_d%27ensemble.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Ancien_Institut_national_de_Radiodiffusion_-_vue_d%27ensemble.JPG/220px-Ancien_Institut_national_de_Radiodiffusion_-_vue_d%27ensemble.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Ancien_Institut_national_de_Radiodiffusion_-_vue_d%27ensemble.JPG/330px-Ancien_Institut_national_de_Radiodiffusion_-_vue_d%27ensemble.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Ancien_Institut_national_de_Radiodiffusion_-_vue_d%27ensemble.JPG/440px-Ancien_Institut_national_de_Radiodiffusion_-_vue_d%27ensemble.JPG 2x" data-file-width="6016" data-file-height="4000" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ancien_Institut_national_de_Radiodiffusion_-_vue_d%27ensemble.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Le_Flagey" title="Le Flagey">Former Belgian National Institute of Radio Broadcasting</a> (or <i>Maison de la Radio</i>) in <a href="/wiki/Ixelles" title="Ixelles">Ixelles</a></div></div></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Atomium" title="Atomium">Atomium</a> is a symbolic 103-metre-tall (338&#160;ft) <a href="/wiki/Modern_architecture" title="Modern architecture">modernist</a> structure, located on the Heysel Plateau, which was originally built for the <a href="/wiki/Expo_%2758" class="mw-redirect" title="Expo &#39;58">1958 World\'s Fair</a> (Expo \'58). It consists of nine steel spheres connected by tubes, and forms a model of an iron crystal (specifically, a <a href="/wiki/Unit_cell" class="mw-redirect" title="Unit cell">unit cell</a>), magnified 165&#160;billion times. The architect <a href="/wiki/Andr%C3%A9_Waterkeyn" title="Andr\xc3\xa9 Waterkeyn">A. Waterkeyn</a> devoted the building to science. It is now considered a <a href="/wiki/Landmark" title="Landmark">landmark</a> of Brussels.<sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">&#91;169&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">&#91;170&#93;</a></sup> Next to the Atomium, is <a href="/wiki/Mini-Europe" title="Mini-Europe">Mini-Europe</a> <a href="/wiki/Miniature_park" title="Miniature park">miniature park</a>, with 1:25 scale <a href="/wiki/Maquette" title="Maquette">maquettes</a> of famous buildings from across Europe.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Atomium_Belgium_1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Atomium_Belgium_1.jpg/220px-Atomium_Belgium_1.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Atomium_Belgium_1.jpg/330px-Atomium_Belgium_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Atomium_Belgium_1.jpg/440px-Atomium_Belgium_1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1200" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Atomium_Belgium_1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Atomium" title="Atomium">Atomium</a>, a landmark of Brussels</div></div></div>\n<p>Since the second half of the 20th century, modern office towers have been built in Brussels (<a href="/wiki/Madou_Plaza_Tower" title="Madou Plaza Tower">Madou Tower</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rogier_Tower" title="Rogier Tower">Rogier Tower</a>, <a href="/wiki/Proximus_Towers" title="Proximus Towers">Proximus Towers</a>, <a href="/wiki/Finance_Tower" title="Finance Tower">Finance Tower</a>, the <a href="/wiki/World_Trade_Center_(Brussels)" title="World Trade Center (Brussels)">World Trade Center</a>, among others). There are some thirty towers, mostly concentrated in the city\'s <a href="/wiki/Central_business_district" title="Central business district">main business district</a>: the <a href="/wiki/Northern_Quarter_(Brussels)" title="Northern Quarter (Brussels)">Northern Quarter</a> (also called <i>Little Manhattan</i>), near <a href="/wiki/Brussels-North_railway_station" title="Brussels-North railway station">Brussels-North railway station</a>. The <a href="/wiki/South_Tower_(Brussels)" class="mw-redirect" title="South Tower (Brussels)">South Tower</a>, standing adjacent to <a href="/wiki/Brussels-South_railway_station" title="Brussels-South railway station">Brussels-South railway station</a>, is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_tallest_structures_in_Belgium" title="List of tallest structures in Belgium">tallest building in Belgium</a>, at 148&#160;m (486&#160;ft). Along the <a href="/wiki/North%E2%80%93South_connection" title="North\xe2\x80\x93South connection">North\xe2\x80\x93South connection</a>, is the State Administrative City, an administrative complex in the <a href="/wiki/International_Style_(architecture)" title="International Style (architecture)">International Style</a>. The postmodern buildings of the <a href="/wiki/Espace_Leopold" class="mw-redirect" title="Espace Leopold">Espace L\xc3\xa9opold</a> complete the picture.\n</p><p>The city\'s embrace of modern architecture translated into an ambivalent approach towards historic preservation, leading to the destruction of notable architectural landmarks, most famously the <a href="/wiki/Maison_du_Peuple_(Brussels)" title="Maison du Peuple (Brussels)"><i>Maison du Peuple</i>/<i>Volkshuis</i></a> by Victor Horta, a process known as <i><a href="/wiki/Brusselization" title="Brusselization">Brusselisation</a></i>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Arts">Arts</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brussels&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Arts">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Brussels_Cinquantenaire_R03.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Brussels_Cinquantenaire_R03.jpg/220px-Brussels_Cinquantenaire_R03.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="152" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Brussels_Cinquantenaire_R03.jpg/330px-Brussels_Cinquantenaire_R03.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Brussels_Cinquantenaire_R03.jpg/440px-Brussels_Cinquantenaire_R03.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3720" data-file-height="2562" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Brussels_Cinquantenaire_R03.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Cinquantenaire_Museum" class="mw-redirect" title="Cinquantenaire Museum">Cinquantenaire/Jubelpark</a> memorial arcade and museums</div></div></div>\n<p>Brussels <a href="/wiki/List_of_museums_in_Brussels" title="List of museums in Brussels">contains over 80 museums</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">&#91;171&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Royal_Museums_of_Fine_Arts_of_Belgium" title="Royal Museums of Fine Arts of Belgium">Royal Museums of Fine Arts</a> has an extensive collection of various painters, such as <a href="/wiki/Flemish_painting" title="Flemish painting">Flemish old masters</a> like <a href="/wiki/Pieter_Bruegel_the_Elder" title="Pieter Bruegel the Elder">Bruegel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rogier_van_der_Weyden" title="Rogier van der Weyden">Rogier van der Weyden</a>, <a href="/wiki/Robert_Campin" title="Robert Campin">Robert Campin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Anthony_van_Dyck" title="Anthony van Dyck">Anthony van Dyck</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jacob_Jordaens" title="Jacob Jordaens">Jacob Jordaens</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Peter_Paul_Rubens" title="Peter Paul Rubens">Peter Paul Rubens</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Magritte_Museum" title="Magritte Museum">Magritte Museum</a> houses the world\'s largest collection of the works of the <a href="/wiki/Surrealism" title="Surrealism">surrealist</a> <a href="/wiki/Ren%C3%A9_Magritte" title="Ren\xc3\xa9 Magritte">Ren\xc3\xa9 Magritte</a>. Museums dedicated to the national history of Belgium include the <a href="/wiki/BELvue_Museum" title="BELvue Museum">BELvue Museum</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Museums_of_Art_and_History" title="Royal Museums of Art and History">Royal Museums of Art and History</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Museum_of_the_Armed_Forces_and_Military_History" title="Royal Museum of the Armed Forces and Military History">Royal Museum of the Armed Forces and Military History</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Musical_Instrument_Museum_(Brussels)" title="Musical Instrument Museum (Brussels)">Musical Instruments Museum</a> (MIM), housed in the <a href="/wiki/Old_England_(department_store)" title="Old England (department store)">Old England</a> building, is part of the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Museums_of_Art_and_History" title="Royal Museums of Art and History">Royal Museums of Art and History</a>, and is internationally renowned for its collection of over 8,000 instruments.\n</p><p>The Brussels Museums Council is an independent body for all the museums in the Brussels-Capital Region, covering around 100 federal, private, municipal, and community museums.<sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176">&#91;172&#93;</a></sup> It promotes member museums through the Brussels Card (giving access to public transport and 30 of the 100 museums), the Brussels Museums Nocturnes (every Thursday from 5 p.m. to 10 p.m. from mid-September to mid-December) and the Museum Night Fever (an event for and by young people on a Saturday night in late February or early March).<sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">&#91;173&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Th%C3%A9%C3%A2tre_de_la_Monnaie_1.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Th%C3%A9%C3%A2tre_de_la_Monnaie_1.JPG/220px-Th%C3%A9%C3%A2tre_de_la_Monnaie_1.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="167" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Th%C3%A9%C3%A2tre_de_la_Monnaie_1.JPG/330px-Th%C3%A9%C3%A2tre_de_la_Monnaie_1.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Th%C3%A9%C3%A2tre_de_la_Monnaie_1.JPG/440px-Th%C3%A9%C3%A2tre_de_la_Monnaie_1.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1318" data-file-height="999" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Th%C3%A9%C3%A2tre_de_la_Monnaie_1.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/La_Monnaie" title="La Monnaie">Royal Theatre of La Monnaie</a></div></div></div>\n<p>Brussels has had a distinguished artist scene for many years. The famous Belgian surrealists <a href="/wiki/Ren%C3%A9_Magritte" title="Ren\xc3\xa9 Magritte">Ren\xc3\xa9 Magritte</a> and <a href="/wiki/Paul_Delvaux" title="Paul Delvaux">Paul Delvaux</a>, for instance, studied and lived there, as did the <a href="/wiki/Avant-garde" title="Avant-garde">avant-garde</a> dramatist <a href="/wiki/Michel_de_Ghelderode" title="Michel de Ghelderode">Michel de Ghelderode</a>. The city was also home of the <a href="/wiki/Impressionism" title="Impressionism">impressionist</a> painter <a href="/wiki/Anna_Boch" title="Anna Boch">Anna Boch</a> from the Artist Group <a href="/wiki/Les_XX" title="Les XX">Les XX</a>, and includes other famous Belgian painters such as <a href="/wiki/L%C3%A9on_Spilliaert" title="L\xc3\xa9on Spilliaert">L\xc3\xa9on Spilliaert</a>. Brussels is also a capital of the <a href="/wiki/Comic_strip" title="Comic strip">comic strip</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-Comic_2-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Comic-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> some treasured Belgian characters are <a href="/wiki/The_Adventures_of_Tintin" title="The Adventures of Tintin">Tintin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lucky_Luke" title="Lucky Luke">Lucky Luke</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_Smurfs" title="The Smurfs">The Smurfs</a>, <a href="/wiki/Spirou_et_Fantasio" class="mw-redirect" title="Spirou et Fantasio">Spirou</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gaston_(comics)" title="Gaston (comics)">Gaston</a>, <a href="/wiki/Marsupilami" title="Marsupilami">Marsupilami</a>, <a href="/wiki/Blake_and_Mortimer" title="Blake and Mortimer">Blake and Mortimer</a>, <a href="/wiki/Boule_et_Bill" title="Boule et Bill">Boule et Bill</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cubitus" title="Cubitus">Cubitus</a> (see <a href="/wiki/Belgian_comics" title="Belgian comics">Belgian comics</a>). Throughout the city, walls are painted with large motifs of comic book characters; these <a href="/wiki/Mural" title="Mural">murals</a> taken together are known as <a href="/wiki/Brussels%27_Comic_Book_Route" title="Brussels&#39; Comic Book Route">Brussels\' Comic Book Route</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_43-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-43">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> Also, the interiors of some <a href="/wiki/Brussels_Metro" title="Brussels Metro">metro stations</a> are designed by artists. The <a href="/wiki/Belgian_Comic_Strip_Center" title="Belgian Comic Strip Center">Belgian Comic Strip Center</a> combines two artistic leitmotifs of Brussels, being a museum devoted to Belgian comic strips, housed in the former <i>Magasins Waucquez</i> textile department store, designed by <a href="/wiki/Victor_Horta" title="Victor Horta">Victor Horta</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Art_Nouveau_in_Brussels" title="Art Nouveau in Brussels">Art Nouveau</a> style.\n</p><p>Brussels is well known for its <a href="/wiki/Performing_arts" title="Performing arts">performing arts</a> scene, with the <a href="/wiki/La_Monnaie" title="La Monnaie">Royal Theatre of La Monnaie</a> and the Kaaitheater among the most notable institutions. The Kunstenfestivaldesarts, an international performing arts festival, is organised every year in May in about twenty different cultural houses and theatres throughout the city.<sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178">&#91;174&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/King_Baudouin_Stadium" title="King Baudouin Stadium">King Baudouin Stadium</a> is a concert and competition facility with a 50,000 seat capacity, the largest in Belgium. The site was formerly occupied by the <a href="/wiki/Heysel_Stadium" class="mw-redirect" title="Heysel Stadium">Heysel Stadium</a>. Furthermore, the <a href="/wiki/Centre_for_Fine_Arts,_Brussels" title="Centre for Fine Arts, Brussels">Center for Fine Arts</a> (often referred to as BOZAR in French or PSK in Dutch), a multi-purpose centre for theatre, cinema, music, literature and art exhibitions, is home to the <a href="/wiki/National_Orchestra_of_Belgium" class="mw-redirect" title="National Orchestra of Belgium">National Orchestra of Belgium</a> and to the annual <a href="/wiki/Queen_Elisabeth_Competition" title="Queen Elisabeth Competition">Queen Elisabeth Competition</a> for <a href="/wiki/Classical_music" title="Classical music">classical</a> singers and instrumentalists, one of the most challenging and prestigious competitions of the kind. Studio 4 in <a href="/wiki/Le_Flagey" title="Le Flagey">Le Flagey</a> cultural centre hosts the <a href="/wiki/Brussels_Philharmonic" title="Brussels Philharmonic">Brussels Philharmonic</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">&#91;175&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180">&#91;176&#93;</a></sup> Other concert venues include <a href="/wiki/Forest_National" title="Forest National">Forest National/Vorst Nationaal</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Ancienne_Belgique" title="Ancienne Belgique">Ancienne Belgique</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Cirque_Royal" title="Cirque Royal">Cirque Royal/Koninklijk Circus</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Le_Botanique" title="Le Botanique">Botanique</a> and <a href="/wiki/Palais_12" title="Palais 12">Palais 12/Paleis 12</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Jazz_Station" title="Jazz Station">Jazz Station</a> in <a href="/wiki/Saint-Josse-ten-Noode" title="Saint-Josse-ten-Noode">Saint-Josse-ten-Noode</a> is a museum and archive on <a href="/wiki/Jazz" title="Jazz">jazz</a>, and a venue for jazz concerts.<sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181">&#91;177&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Folklore">Folklore</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brussels&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Folklore">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:GeantsMeyboom2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/GeantsMeyboom2.jpg/170px-GeantsMeyboom2.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/GeantsMeyboom2.jpg/255px-GeantsMeyboom2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/GeantsMeyboom2.jpg/340px-GeantsMeyboom2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="800" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:GeantsMeyboom2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Meyboom" title="Meyboom">Meyboom</a> giants in Brussels, a <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a> <a href="/wiki/Intangible_cultural_heritage" title="Intangible cultural heritage">Intangible Cultural Heritage</a></div></div></div>\n<p>Brussels\' identity owes much to its rich folklore and traditions, among the liveliest in the country.\n</p>\n<ul><li>The <a href="/wiki/Ommegang_of_Brussels" title="Ommegang of Brussels">Ommegang</a>, a folkloric costumed procession, commemorating the <a href="/wiki/Joyous_Entry" title="Joyous Entry">Joyous Entry</a> of <a href="/wiki/Charles_V,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Charles V, Holy Roman Emperor">Emperor Charles V</a> in the city in 1549, takes place every year in July. The colourful parade includes floats, traditional giant puppets, such as <a href="/wiki/Saint_Michael" class="mw-redirect" title="Saint Michael">Saint Michael</a> and <a href="/wiki/Saint_Gudula" class="mw-redirect" title="Saint Gudula">Saint Gudula</a>, and scores of folkloric groups, either on foot or on horseback, dressed in medieval garb. The parade ends in a <a href="/wiki/Medieval_pageant" title="Medieval pageant">pageant</a> on the <a href="/wiki/Grand_Place" title="Grand Place">Grand Place</a>.</li>\n<li>The <a href="/wiki/Meyboom" title="Meyboom">Meyboom</a>, an even-older folk tradition of Brussels (1308), celebrating the May tree\xe2\x80\x94in fact, a bad translation of the Dutch <i>tree of joy</i>\xe2\x80\x94takes place paradoxically on 9 August. After parading a young <a href="/wiki/Beech" title="Beech">beech</a> in the city, it is planted in a joyful spirit with lots of music, <i>Brusseleir</i> songs, and giant puppets. It was recognised as an expression of <a href="/wiki/Intangible_cultural_heritage" title="Intangible cultural heritage">intangible cultural heritage</a> by <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a>, as part of the bi-national inscription "<a href="/wiki/Processional_giants_and_dragons_in_Belgium_and_France" title="Processional giants and dragons in Belgium and France">Processional giants and dragons in Belgium and France</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182">&#91;178&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183">&#91;179&#93;</a></sup> The celebration is reminiscent of the town\'s long-standing (folkloric) feud with <a href="/wiki/Leuven" title="Leuven">Leuven</a>, which dates back to the <a href="/wiki/Middle_Ages" title="Middle Ages">Middle Ages</a>.</li>\n<li>Another good introduction to the <i>Brusseleir</i> <a href="/wiki/Marols" title="Marols">local dialect</a> and way of life can be obtained at the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Theatre_Toone" title="Royal Theatre Toone">Royal Theatre Toone</a>, a folkloric theatre of <a href="/wiki/Marionette" title="Marionette">marionettes</a>, located a stone\'s throw away from the Grand Place.<sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184">&#91;180&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>The <a href="/wiki/St_V" title="St V">Saint-Verhaegen</a> (often shortened to <i>St V</i>), a folkloric student procession, celebrating the anniversary of the founding of the <a href="/wiki/Universit%C3%A9_libre_de_Bruxelles" title="Universit\xc3\xa9 libre de Bruxelles">Universit\xc3\xa9 libre de Bruxelles</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Vrije_Universiteit_Brussel" title="Vrije Universiteit Brussel">Vrije Universiteit Brussel</a>, is held on 20 November.</li></ul>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cultural_events_and_festivals">Cultural events and festivals</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brussels&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Cultural events and festivals">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Brussels_Summer_Festival_(4890801736).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Brussels_Summer_Festival_%284890801736%29.jpg/220px-Brussels_Summer_Festival_%284890801736%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Brussels_Summer_Festival_%284890801736%29.jpg/330px-Brussels_Summer_Festival_%284890801736%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Brussels_Summer_Festival_%284890801736%29.jpg/440px-Brussels_Summer_Festival_%284890801736%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4288" data-file-height="2848" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Brussels_Summer_Festival_(4890801736).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Brussels Summer Festival</div></div></div>\n<p>Many events are organised or hosted in Brussels throughout the year. In addition, many festivals animate the Brussels scene.\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Iris_Festival" title="Iris Festival">Iris Festival</a> is the official festival of the Brussels-Capital Region and is held annually in spring.<sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185">&#91;181&#93;</a></sup> The International Fantastic Film Festival of Brussels (BIFFF) is organised during the Easter holidays<sup id="cite_ref-186" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-186">&#91;182&#93;</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Magritte_Award" class="mw-redirect" title="Magritte Award">Magritte Awards</a> in February. The <a href="/wiki/Festival_of_Europe" class="mw-redirect" title="Festival of Europe">Festival of Europe</a>, an open day and activities in and around the institutions of the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a>, is held on 9 May. On <a href="/wiki/Belgian_National_Day" title="Belgian National Day">Belgian National Day</a>, on 21 July, a military parade and celebrations take place on the <span lang="fr" style="font-style: normal;" title="French-language text">Place des Palais</span>/<span lang="nl" style="font-style: normal;" title="Dutch-language text">Paleizenplein</span> and in <a href="/wiki/Brussels_Park" class="mw-redirect" title="Brussels Park">Brussels\' Park</a>, ending with a display of fireworks in the evening.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Zinneke-parade-brussel-1350316079.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Zinneke-parade-brussel-1350316079.jpg/220px-Zinneke-parade-brussel-1350316079.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Zinneke-parade-brussel-1350316079.jpg/330px-Zinneke-parade-brussel-1350316079.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Zinneke-parade-brussel-1350316079.jpg/440px-Zinneke-parade-brussel-1350316079.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="480" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Zinneke-parade-brussel-1350316079.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Zinneke_Parade" title="Zinneke Parade">Zinneke Parade</a></div></div></div>\n<p>Some summer festivities include <a href="/wiki/Couleur_Caf%C3%A9" title="Couleur Caf\xc3\xa9">Couleur Caf\xc3\xa9 Festival</a>, a festival of <a href="/wiki/World_music" title="World music">world</a> and <a href="/wiki/Urban_contemporary" title="Urban contemporary">urban music</a>, around the end of June or early July, the Brussels Summer Festival (BSF), a music festival in August,<sup id="cite_ref-187" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-187">&#91;183&#93;</a></sup> the Brussels Fair, the most important yearly fair in Brussels, lasting more than a month, in July and August,<sup id="cite_ref-188" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-188">&#91;184&#93;</a></sup> and Brussels Beach, when the banks of the <a href="/wiki/Brussels%E2%80%93Charleroi_Canal" title="Brussels\xe2\x80\x93Charleroi Canal">canal</a> are turned into a temporary urban beach.<sup id="cite_ref-189" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-189">&#91;185&#93;</a></sup> Other biennial events are the <a href="/wiki/Zinneke_Parade" title="Zinneke Parade">Zinneke Parade</a>, a colourful, multicultural parade through the city, which has been held since 2000 in May, as well as the popular <a href="/wiki/Flower_Carpet_(Brussels)" title="Flower Carpet (Brussels)">Flower Carpet</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Grand_Place" title="Grand Place">Grand Place</a> in August. <a href="/wiki/European_Heritage_Days" title="European Heritage Days">Heritage Days</a> are organised on the third weekend of September (sometimes coinciding with the car-free day) and are a good opportunity to discover the wealth of buildings, institutions and real estate in Brussels. The "Winter Wonders" animate the heart of Brussels in December; these winter activities were launched in Brussels in 2001.<sup id="cite_ref-190" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-190">&#91;186&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cuisine">Cuisine</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brussels&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Cuisine">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Brussels_waffle.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Brussels_waffle.jpg/170px-Brussels_waffle.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="255" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Brussels_waffle.jpg/255px-Brussels_waffle.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Brussels_waffle.jpg/340px-Brussels_waffle.jpg 2x" data-file-width="853" data-file-height="1280" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Brussels_waffle.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Brussels is known for its local <a href="/wiki/Belgian_waffle" title="Belgian waffle">waffles</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>Brussels is known for its local <a href="/wiki/Belgian_waffle" title="Belgian waffle">waffle</a>, its <a href="/wiki/Chocolate" title="Chocolate">chocolate</a>, its <a href="/wiki/French_fries" title="French fries">French fries</a> and its numerous types of <a href="/wiki/Beer" title="Beer">beers</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Brussels_sprout" title="Brussels sprout">Brussels sprout</a>, which has long been popular in Brussels, and may have originated there, is also named after the city.<sup id="cite_ref-191" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-191">&#91;187&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The gastronomic offer includes approximately 1,800 <a href="/wiki/Restaurant" title="Restaurant">restaurants</a> (including three 2-starred and ten 1-starred <a href="/wiki/Michelin_Guide" title="Michelin Guide">Michelin</a> restaurants),<sup id="cite_ref-192" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-192">&#91;188&#93;</a></sup> and a number of bars. In addition to the traditional restaurants, there are many <a href="/wiki/Coffeehouse" title="Coffeehouse">caf\xc3\xa9s</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bistro" title="Bistro">bistros</a> and the usual range of international <a href="/wiki/Fast_food_restaurant" title="Fast food restaurant">fast food</a> chains. The caf\xc3\xa9s are similar to bars, and offer beer and light dishes; <a href="/wiki/Coffeehouse" title="Coffeehouse">coffee houses</a> are called <i lang="fr" title="French-language text">salons de th\xc3\xa9</i>. Also widespread are <a href="/wiki/Brasserie" title="Brasserie">brasseries</a>, which usually offer a variety of beers and typical national dishes.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Belgian_cuisine" title="Belgian cuisine">Belgian cuisine</a> is known among connoisseurs as one of the best in Europe. It is characterised by the combination of <a href="/wiki/French_cuisine" title="French cuisine">French cuisine</a> with the more hearty Flemish fare. Notable specialities include <a href="/wiki/Brussels_waffle" class="mw-redirect" title="Brussels waffle">Brussels waffles</a> (gaufres) and <a href="/wiki/Mussels" class="mw-redirect" title="Mussels">mussels</a> (usually as <a href="/wiki/Moules_frites" class="mw-redirect" title="Moules frites"><i>moules-frites</i></a>, served with fries).
