The city is a stronghold of <a href="/wiki/Chocolate" title="Chocolate">chocolate</a> and <a href="/wiki/Praline" title="Praline">pralines</a> manufacturers with renowned companies like <a href="/wiki/C%C3%B4te_d%27Or_(chocolate)" title="C\xc3\xb4te d&#39;Or (chocolate)">C\xc3\xb4te d\'Or</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chocolatier_Neuhaus" class="mw-redirect" title="Chocolatier Neuhaus">Neuhaus</a>, <a href="/wiki/Leonidas_(chocolate_maker)" title="Leonidas (chocolate maker)">Leonidas</a> and <a href="/wiki/Godiva_Chocolatier" title="Godiva Chocolatier">Godiva</a>. Pralines were first introduced in 1912, by Jean Neuhaus II, a Belgian <a href="/wiki/Chocolatier" title="Chocolatier">chocolatier</a> of Swiss origin, in the Royal Saint-Hubert Galleries.<sup id="cite_ref-193" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-193">&#91;189&#93;</a></sup> Numerous <a href="/wiki/Friteries" class="mw-redirect" title="Friteries">friteries</a> are spread throughout the city, and in tourist areas, fresh hot waffles are also sold on the street.\n</p><p>As well as other <a href="/wiki/Beer_in_Belgium" title="Beer in Belgium">Belgian beers</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Spontaneous_fermentation" class="mw-redirect" title="Spontaneous fermentation">spontaneously fermented</a> <a href="/wiki/Lambic" title="Lambic">lambic</a> style, brewed in and around Brussels, is widely available there and in the nearby <a href="/wiki/Zenne" class="mw-redirect" title="Zenne">Senne</a> valley where the wild yeasts which ferment it have their origin. <a href="/wiki/Kriek_lambic" title="Kriek lambic">Kriek</a>, a cherry lambic, is available in almost every bar or restaurant in Brussels.\n</p><p>Brussels is known as the birthplace of the <a href="/wiki/Chicory" title="Chicory">Belgian endive</a>. The technique for growing <a href="/wiki/Blanching_(horticulture)" title="Blanching (horticulture)">blanched</a> endives was accidentally discovered in the 1850s at the <a href="/wiki/Botanical_Garden_of_Brussels" title="Botanical Garden of Brussels">Botanical Garden of Brussels</a> in <a href="/wiki/Saint-Josse-ten-Noode" title="Saint-Josse-ten-Noode">Saint-Josse-ten-Noode</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-194" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-194">&#91;190&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Shopping">Shopping</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brussels&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Shopping">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:107_-_March%C3%A9_aux_puces_place_du_Jeu_de_Balle_-_Bruxelles.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/107_-_March%C3%A9_aux_puces_place_du_Jeu_de_Balle_-_Bruxelles.jpg/220px-107_-_March%C3%A9_aux_puces_place_du_Jeu_de_Balle_-_Bruxelles.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/107_-_March%C3%A9_aux_puces_place_du_Jeu_de_Balle_-_Bruxelles.jpg/330px-107_-_March%C3%A9_aux_puces_place_du_Jeu_de_Balle_-_Bruxelles.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/107_-_March%C3%A9_aux_puces_place_du_Jeu_de_Balle_-_Bruxelles.jpg/440px-107_-_March%C3%A9_aux_puces_place_du_Jeu_de_Balle_-_Bruxelles.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3456" data-file-height="2304" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:107_-_March%C3%A9_aux_puces_place_du_Jeu_de_Balle_-_Bruxelles.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Flea_market" title="Flea market">Flea Market</a> on the <a href="/wiki/Place_du_Jeu_de_Balle" title="Place du Jeu de Balle">Place du Jeu de Balle/Vossenplein</a></div></div></div>\n<p>Famous <a href="/wiki/Shopping" title="Shopping">shopping</a> areas in Brussels include the pedestrian-only <a href="/wiki/Rue_Neuve_(Brussels)" class="mw-redirect" title="Rue Neuve (Brussels)">Rue Neuve/Nieuwstraat</a>, the second busiest shopping street in Belgium (after the <a href="/wiki/Meir,_Antwerp" title="Meir, Antwerp">Meir</a>, in <a href="/wiki/Antwerp" title="Antwerp">Antwerp</a>) with a weekly average of 230,000 visitors,<sup id="cite_ref-195" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-195">&#91;191&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-196" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-196">&#91;192&#93;</a></sup> home to popular international chains (<a href="/wiki/H%26M" title="H&amp;M">H&amp;M</a>, <a href="/wiki/C%26A" title="C&amp;A">C&amp;A</a>, <a href="/wiki/Zara_(retailer)" title="Zara (retailer)">Zara</a>, <a href="/wiki/Primark" title="Primark">Primark</a>), as well as the City 2 and Anspach galleries.<sup id="cite_ref-:3_197-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:3-197">&#91;193&#93;</a></sup> The Royal Saint-Hubert Galleries hold a variety of luxury shops and some six million people stroll through them each year.<sup id="cite_ref-198" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-198">&#91;194&#93;</a></sup> The neighbourhood around <span lang="fr" style="font-style: normal;" title="French-language text">Rue Antoine Dansaert</span>/<span lang="nl" style="font-style: normal;" title="Dutch-language text">Antoine Dansaertstraat</span> has become, in recent years, a focal point for fashion and design;<sup id="cite_ref-199" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-199">&#91;195&#93;</a></sup> this main street and its side streets also feature Belgium\'s young and most happening artistic talent.<sup id="cite_ref-200" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-200">&#91;196&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In Ixelles, <span lang="fr" style="font-style: normal;" title="French-language text">Avenue de la Toison d\'Or</span>/<span lang="nl" style="font-style: normal;" title="Dutch-language text">Gulden-Vlieslaan</span> and <a href="/wiki/Namur_Gate" title="Namur Gate">Namur Gate</a> area offer a blend of luxury shops, fast food restaurants and entertainment venues, and <span lang="fr" style="font-style: normal;" title="French-language text">Chauss\xc3\xa9e d\'Ixelles</span>/<span lang="nl" style="font-style: normal;" title="Dutch-language text">Elsenesteenweg</span>, in the mainly-Congolese <i><a href="/wiki/Matong%C3%A9_(Ixelles)" class="mw-redirect" title="Matong\xc3\xa9 (Ixelles)">Matong\xc3\xa9</a></i> district, offers a great taste of African fashion and lifestyle. The nearby <a href="/wiki/Avenue_Louise" title="Avenue Louise">Avenue Louise</a> is lined with high-end fashion stores and boutiques, making it one of the most expensive streets in Belgium.<sup id="cite_ref-201" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-201">&#91;197&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>There are shopping centres outside the inner ring: Basilix, Woluwe Shopping Center, Westland Shopping Center, and Docks Bruxsel, which opened in October 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-:3_197-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:3-197">&#91;193&#93;</a></sup> In addition, Brussels ranks as one of Europe\'s best capital cities for <a href="/wiki/Flea_market" title="Flea market">flea market</a> shopping. The<i> Old Market</i>, on the <a href="/wiki/Place_du_Jeu_de_Balle" title="Place du Jeu de Balle">Place du Jeu de Balle/Vossenplein</a>, in the <a href="/wiki/Marollen" title="Marollen"><i>Marolles</i>/<i>Marollen</i></a> neighbourhood, is particularly renowned.<sup id="cite_ref-202" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-202">&#91;198&#93;</a></sup> The nearby <a href="/wiki/Sablon_(Brussels)" class="mw-redirect" title="Sablon (Brussels)"><i>Sablon</i>/<i>Zavel</i></a> area is home to many of Brussels\' <a href="/wiki/Antique" title="Antique">antique</a> dealers.<sup id="cite_ref-203" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-203">&#91;199&#93;</a></sup> The <i>Midi Market</i> around <a href="/wiki/Brussels-South_railway_station" title="Brussels-South railway station">Brussels-South station</a> and <span lang="fr" style="font-style: normal;" title="French-language text">Boulevard du Midi</span>/<span lang="nl" style="font-style: normal;" title="Dutch-language text">Zuidlaan</span> is reputed to be one of the largest markets in Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-204" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-204">&#91;200&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brussels&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Sports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Sport_in_Belgium" title="Sport in Belgium">Sport in Belgium</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:20_km_de_Bruxelles.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/20_km_de_Bruxelles.jpg/220px-20_km_de_Bruxelles.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/20_km_de_Bruxelles.jpg/330px-20_km_de_Bruxelles.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/20_km_de_Bruxelles.jpg/440px-20_km_de_Bruxelles.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3552" data-file-height="2368" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:20_km_de_Bruxelles.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/20_km_of_Brussels" title="20 km of Brussels">20 km of Brussels</a></div></div></div>\n<p>Sport in Brussels is under the responsibility of the <a href="/wiki/Communities,_regions_and_language_areas_of_Belgium" title="Communities, regions and language areas of Belgium">Communities</a>. The <i lang="fr" title="French-language text">Administration de l\'\xc3\x89ducation Physique et du Sport</i> (<a href="/wiki/ADEPS" title="ADEPS">ADEPS</a>) is responsible for recognising the various French-speaking sports federations and also runs three sports centres in the Brussels-Capital Region.<sup id="cite_ref-205" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-205">&#91;201&#93;</a></sup> Its Dutch-speaking counterpart is <i lang="nl" title="Dutch-language text">Sport Vlaanderen</i> (formerly called <a href="/wiki/Bloso" class="mw-redirect" title="Bloso">BLOSO</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-206" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-206">&#91;202&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/King_Baudouin_Stadium" title="King Baudouin Stadium">King Baudouin Stadium</a> (formerly Heysel Stadium) is the largest in the country and home to the national teams in <a href="/wiki/Belgium_national_football_team" title="Belgium national football team">football</a> and <a href="/wiki/Belgium_national_rugby_union_team" title="Belgium national rugby union team">rugby union</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-207" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-207">&#91;203&#93;</a></sup> It hosted the final of the <a href="/wiki/1972_UEFA_European_Football_Championship" class="mw-redirect" title="1972 UEFA European Football Championship">1972 UEFA European Football Championship</a>, and the opening game of <a href="/wiki/Euro_2000" class="mw-redirect" title="Euro 2000">the 2000 edition</a>. Several European club finals have been held at the ground, including the <a href="/wiki/1985_European_Cup_Final" title="1985 European Cup Final">1985 European Cup Final</a> which saw 39 deaths due to hooliganism and structural collapse.<sup id="cite_ref-208" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-208">&#91;204&#93;</a></sup> The King Baudouin Stadium is also home of the annual <a href="/wiki/Memorial_Van_Damme" title="Memorial Van Damme">Memorial Van Damme</a> athletics event, Belgium\'s foremost <a href="/wiki/Track_and_field" title="Track and field">track and field</a> competition, which is part of the <a href="/wiki/Diamond_League" title="Diamond League">Diamond League</a>. Other important athletics events are the <a href="/wiki/Brussels_Marathon" title="Brussels Marathon">Brussels Marathon</a> and the <a href="/wiki/20_km_of_Brussels" title="20 km of Brussels">20 km of Brussels</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cycling">Cycling</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brussels&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Cycling">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Brussels is home to notable <a href="/wiki/Cycling_race" class="mw-redirect" title="Cycling race">cycling races</a>. The city is the arrival location of the <a href="/wiki/Brussels_Cycling_Classic" title="Brussels Cycling Classic">Brussels Cycling Classic</a>, formerly known as Paris\xe2\x80\x93Brussels, which is one of the oldest <a href="/wiki/Classic_cycle_races" title="Classic cycle races">semi classic</a> <a href="/wiki/Road_bicycle_racing" title="Road bicycle racing">bicycle races</a> on the international calendar. From World War I until the early 1970s, the <a href="/wiki/Six_Days_of_Brussels" title="Six Days of Brussels">Six Days of Brussels</a> was organised regularly. In the last decades of the 20th century, the <a href="/wiki/Grand_Prix_Eddy_Merckx" title="Grand Prix Eddy Merckx">Grand Prix Eddy Merckx</a> was also held in Brussels.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Association_football">Association football</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brussels&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Association football">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Constant_Vanden_Stockstadion,_Anderlecht.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/Constant_Vanden_Stockstadion%2C_Anderlecht.jpg/220px-Constant_Vanden_Stockstadion%2C_Anderlecht.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="158" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/Constant_Vanden_Stockstadion%2C_Anderlecht.jpg/330px-Constant_Vanden_Stockstadion%2C_Anderlecht.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/Constant_Vanden_Stockstadion%2C_Anderlecht.jpg/440px-Constant_Vanden_Stockstadion%2C_Anderlecht.jpg 2x" data-file-width="556" data-file-height="400" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Constant_Vanden_Stockstadion,_Anderlecht.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/R.S.C._Anderlecht" title="R.S.C. Anderlecht">R.S.C. Anderlecht</a> fans at the <a href="/wiki/Lotto_Park" title="Lotto Park">Lotto Park</a></div></div></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/R.S.C._Anderlecht" title="R.S.C. Anderlecht">R.S.C. Anderlecht</a>, based in the <a href="/wiki/Constant_Vanden_Stock_Stadium" class="mw-redirect" title="Constant Vanden Stock Stadium">Constant Vanden Stock Stadium</a> in <a href="/wiki/Anderlecht" title="Anderlecht">Anderlecht</a>, is the most successful Belgian football club in the <a href="/wiki/Belgian_Pro_League" class="mw-redirect" title="Belgian Pro League">Belgian Pro League</a>, with 34 titles.<sup id="cite_ref-209" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-209">&#91;205&#93;</a></sup> It has also won the most major European tournaments for a Belgian side, with 6 European titles.\n</p><p>Brussels is also home to <a href="/wiki/R._Union_Saint-Gilloise" class="mw-redirect" title="R. Union Saint-Gilloise">Union Saint-Gilloise</a>, the most successful Belgian club before World War II, with 11 titles<sup id="cite_ref-210" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-210">&#91;206&#93;</a></sup> The club was founded in <a href="/wiki/Saint-Gilles,_Belgium" title="Saint-Gilles, Belgium">Saint-Gilles</a> but is based in nearby <a href="/wiki/Forest,_Belgium" title="Forest, Belgium">Forest</a>, and plays in the <a href="/wiki/Belgian_Second_Division" title="Belgian Second Division">Second Division</a>. <a href="/wiki/R._White_Star_Bruxelles" class="mw-redirect" title="R. White Star Bruxelles">White Star Bruxelles</a> is another football club that plays in second division. <a href="/wiki/R._White_Daring_Molenbeek" class="mw-redirect" title="R. White Daring Molenbeek">Racing White Daring Molenbeek</a>, based in <a href="/wiki/Molenbeek-Saint-Jean" title="Molenbeek-Saint-Jean">Molenbeek-Saint-Jean</a>, and often referred to as RWDM, was a very popular football club until it was dissolved in 2002. Since 2015, its reincarnation <a href="/wiki/RWDM47" title="RWDM47">RWDM47</a> is back playing in the second division.\n</p><p>Other Brussels clubs that played in the national series over the years were Ixelles SC, <a href="/wiki/K.V.V._Crossing_Elewijt" title="K.V.V. Crossing Elewijt">Crossing Club de Schaerbeek</a> (born from a merger between RCS de Schaerbeek and Crossing Club Molenbeek), Scup Jette, RUS de Laeken, Racing Jet de Bruxelles, AS Auderghem, KV Wosjot Woluwe and FC Ganshoren.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brussels&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Belgium" title="Economy of Belgium">Economy of Belgium</a></div>\n<p>Serving as the centre of administration for Belgium and Europe, Brussels\' economy is largely <a href="/wiki/Tertiary_sector_of_the_economy" title="Tertiary sector of the economy">service</a>-oriented. It is dominated by regional and world headquarters of <a href="/wiki/Multinational_corporation" title="Multinational corporation">multinationals</a>, by European institutions, by various local and federal administrations, and by related services companies, though it does have a number of notable <a href="/wiki/Craft" title="Craft">craft</a> industries, such as the <a href="/wiki/Cantillon_Brewery" class="mw-redirect" title="Cantillon Brewery">Cantillon Brewery</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Lambic" title="Lambic">lambic</a> brewery founded in 1900.<sup id="cite_ref-211" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-211">&#91;207&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:North_Galaxy_Towers-Schaerbeek-001.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/North_Galaxy_Towers-Schaerbeek-001.JPG/220px-North_Galaxy_Towers-Schaerbeek-001.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/North_Galaxy_Towers-Schaerbeek-001.JPG/330px-North_Galaxy_Towers-Schaerbeek-001.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/North_Galaxy_Towers-Schaerbeek-001.JPG/440px-North_Galaxy_Towers-Schaerbeek-001.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3648" data-file-height="2736" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:North_Galaxy_Towers-Schaerbeek-001.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Brussels\' <a href="/wiki/Northern_Quarter_(Brussels)" title="Northern Quarter (Brussels)">Northern Quarter</a> business district</div></div></div>\n<p>Brussels has a robust economy. The region contributes to one fifth of Belgium\'s <a href="/wiki/Gross_domestic_product" title="Gross domestic product">GDP</a>, and its 550,000 jobs account for 17.7% of Belgium\'s employment.<sup id="cite_ref-212" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-212">&#91;208&#93;</a></sup> Its <a href="/wiki/GDP_per_capita" class="mw-redirect" title="GDP per capita">GDP per capita</a> is nearly double that of Belgium as a whole,<sup id="cite_ref-:4_16-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:4-16">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> and it has the highest GDP per capita of any <a href="/wiki/Nomenclature_of_Territorial_Units_for_Statistics" title="Nomenclature of Territorial Units for Statistics">NUTS 1</a> region in the EU, at ~$80,000 in 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-213" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-213">&#91;209&#93;</a></sup> That being said, the GDP is boosted by a massive inflow of <a href="/wiki/Commuting" title="Commuting">commuters</a> from neighbouring regions; over half of those who work in Brussels live in Flanders or Wallonia, with 230,000 and 130,000 commuters per day respectively. Conversely, only 16.0% of people from Brussels work outside Brussels (68,827 (68.5%) of them in Flanders and 21,035 (31.5%) in Wallonia).<sup id="cite_ref-214" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-214">&#91;210&#93;</a></sup> Not all of the wealth generated in Brussels remains in Brussels itself, and as of December&#160;2013<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Brussels&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, the unemployment among residents of Brussels is 20.4%.<sup id="cite_ref-215" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-215">&#91;211&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bourse_Bxl_02.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Bourse_Bxl_02.JPG/220px-Bourse_Bxl_02.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="170" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Bourse_Bxl_02.JPG/330px-Bourse_Bxl_02.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Bourse_Bxl_02.JPG/440px-Bourse_Bxl_02.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2224" data-file-height="1714" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bourse_Bxl_02.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The former <a href="/wiki/Brussels_Stock_Exchange" title="Brussels Stock Exchange">Brussels Stock Exchange</a> building</div></div></div>\n<p>There are approximately 50,000 <a href="/wiki/Business" title="Business">businesses</a> in Brussels, of which around 2,200 are foreign. This number is constantly increasing and can well explain the role of Brussels in Europe. The city\'s <a href="/wiki/Infrastructure" title="Infrastructure">infrastructure</a> is very favourable in terms of starting up a new business. House prices have also increased in recent years, especially with the increase of young <a href="/wiki/Professional" title="Professional">professionals</a> settling down in Brussels, making it the most expensive city to live in Belgium.<sup id="cite_ref-216" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-216">&#91;212&#93;</a></sup> In addition, Brussels holds more than 1,000 business conferences annually, making it the ninth most popular conference city in Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-217" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-217">&#91;213&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Brussels is rated as the 34th most important financial centre in the world as of 2020, according to the <a href="/wiki/Global_Financial_Centres_Index" title="Global Financial Centres Index">Global Financial Centres Index</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Brussels_Stock_Exchange" title="Brussels Stock Exchange">Brussels Stock Exchange</a>, abbreviated to BSE, now called <i>Euronext Brussels</i>, is part of the European <a href="/wiki/Stock_exchange" title="Stock exchange">stock exchange</a> <a href="/wiki/Euronext_N.V." class="mw-redirect" title="Euronext N.V.">Euronext N.V.</a>, along with <a href="/wiki/Paris_Bourse" class="mw-redirect" title="Paris Bourse">Paris Bourse</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lisbon_Stock_Exchange" class="mw-redirect" title="Lisbon Stock Exchange">Lisbon Stock Exchange</a> and <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam_Stock_Exchange" class="mw-redirect" title="Amsterdam Stock Exchange">Amsterdam Stock Exchange</a>. Its benchmark <a href="/wiki/Stock_market_index" title="Stock market index">stock market index</a> is the <a href="/wiki/BEL20" class="mw-redirect" title="BEL20">BEL20</a>.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brussels&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Belgian_media" class="mw-redirect" title="Belgian media">Belgian media</a></div>\n<p>Brussels is a centre of both media and communications in Belgium, with many Belgian television stations, radio stations, <a href="/wiki/Newspaper" title="Newspaper">newspapers</a> and telephone companies having their headquarters in the region. The Belgian French-language <a href="/wiki/Public_broadcasting" title="Public broadcasting">public broadcaster</a> <a href="/wiki/RTBF" title="RTBF">RTBF</a>, the Belgian Dutch-speaking public broadcaster <a href="/wiki/Vlaamse_Radio-_en_Televisieomroeporganisatie" class="mw-redirect" title="Vlaamse Radio- en Televisieomroeporganisatie">VRT</a>, the two regional channels BX1 (formerly <i>T\xc3\xa9l\xc3\xa9 Bruxelles</i>)<sup id="cite_ref-218" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-218">&#91;214&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Bruzz" title="Bruzz">Bruzz</a> (formerly <i>TV Brussel</i>),<sup id="cite_ref-219" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-219">&#91;215&#93;</a></sup> the encrypted <a href="/wiki/BeTV_(Belgium)" title="BeTV (Belgium)">BeTV</a> channel and private channels <a href="/wiki/RTL-TVI" title="RTL-TVI">RTL-TVI</a> and <a href="/wiki/VTM_(TV_channel)" title="VTM (TV channel)">VTM</a> are headquartered in Brussels. Some national newspapers such as <a href="/wiki/Le_Soir" title="Le Soir">Le Soir</a>, <a href="/wiki/La_Libre_Belgique" title="La Libre Belgique">La Libre</a>, <a href="/wiki/De_Morgen" title="De Morgen">De Morgen</a> and the <a href="/wiki/News_agency" title="News agency">news agency</a> <a href="/wiki/Belga_(news_agency)" title="Belga (news agency)">Belga</a> are based in or around Brussels. The Belgian <a href="/wiki/Mail" title="Mail">postal</a> company <a href="/wiki/Bpost" title="Bpost">Bpost</a>, as well as the telecommunication companies and mobile operators <a href="/wiki/Proximus" title="Proximus">Proximus</a>, <a href="/wiki/Orange_Belgium" title="Orange Belgium">Orange Belgium</a> and <a href="/wiki/Telenet_(Belgium)" title="Telenet (Belgium)">Telenet</a> are all located there.\n</p><p>As English is spoken widely,<sup id="cite_ref-BruS13EN_38-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BruS13EN-38">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:7_40-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:7-40">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> several English media organisations operate in Brussels. The most popular of these are the English-language daily news media platform and bi-monthly magazine <i><a href="/wiki/The_Brussels_Times" title="The Brussels Times">The Brussels Times</a></i> and the quarterly magazine and website <i><a href="/wiki/The_Bulletin_(Brussels_weekly)" class="mw-redirect" title="The Bulletin (Brussels weekly)">The Bulletin</a></i>. The <a href="/wiki/Multilingualism" title="Multilingualism">multilingual</a> <a href="/wiki/Pan-European_identity" title="Pan-European identity">pan-European</a> news channel <a href="/wiki/Euronews" title="Euronews">Euronews</a> also maintains an office in Brussels.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brussels&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Belgium" title="Education in Belgium">Education in Belgium</a></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tertiary_education">Tertiary education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brussels&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: Tertiary education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:ULB_20050712.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/ULB_20050712.jpg/170px-ULB_20050712.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="213" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/ULB_20050712.jpg/255px-ULB_20050712.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/ULB_20050712.jpg/340px-ULB_20050712.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="800" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:ULB_20050712.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The main building on the <i>Solbosch</i> campus of the <a href="/wiki/Universit%C3%A9_libre_de_Bruxelles" title="Universit\xc3\xa9 libre de Bruxelles">Universit\xc3\xa9 libre de Bruxelles</a></div></div></div>\n<p>There are several <a href="/wiki/University" title="University">universities</a> in Brussels. Except for the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Military_Academy_(Belgium)" title="Royal Military Academy (Belgium)">Royal Military Academy</a>, a military college established in 1834,<sup id="cite_ref-220" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-220">&#91;216&#93;</a></sup> all universities in Brussels are private/autonomous.\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Universit%C3%A9_Libre_de_Bruxelles" class="mw-redirect" title="Universit\xc3\xa9 Libre de Bruxelles">Universit\xc3\xa9 libre de Bruxelles</a> (ULB), a French-speaking university, with about 20,000 students, has three campuses in the city,<sup id="cite_ref-221" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-221">&#91;217&#93;</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Vrije_Universiteit_Brussel" title="Vrije Universiteit Brussel">Vrije Universiteit Brussel</a> (VUB), its <a href="/wiki/Dutch_language" title="Dutch language">Dutch-speaking</a> sister university, has about 10,000 students.<sup id="cite_ref-222" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-222">&#91;218&#93;</a></sup> Both universities originate from a single ancestor university, founded in 1834, namely the <a href="/wiki/Free_University_of_Brussels_(1834%E2%80%931969)" title="Free University of Brussels (1834\xe2\x80\x931969)">Free University of Brussels</a>, which was split in 1970, at about the same time the Flemish and French Communities gained legislative power over the organisation of higher education.<sup id="cite_ref-223" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-223">&#91;219&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Saint-Louis_University,_Brussels" title="Saint-Louis University, Brussels">Saint-Louis University, Brussels</a> (also known as UCLouvain Saint-Louis \xe2\x80\x93 Bruxelles) was founded in 1858 and is specialised in social and human sciences, with 4,000 students, and located on two campuses in the <a href="/wiki/City_of_Brussels" title="City of Brussels">City of Brussels</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ixelles" title="Ixelles">Ixelles</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-224" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-224">&#91;220&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Still other universities have campuses in Brussels, such as the French-speaking <a href="/wiki/UCLouvain" class="mw-redirect" title="UCLouvain">University of Louvain</a> (UCLouvain), which has 10,000 students in the city with its medical faculties at <a href="/wiki/UCLouvain_Brussels_Woluwe" title="UCLouvain Brussels Woluwe">UCLouvain Bruxelles Woluwe</a> since 1973,<sup id="cite_ref-225" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-225">&#91;221&#93;</a></sup> in addition to its <a href="/wiki/UCLouvain_Faculty_of_Architecture,_Architectural_Engineering_and_Urban_Planning" title="UCLouvain Faculty of Architecture, Architectural Engineering and Urban Planning">Faculty of Architecture, Architectural Engineering and Urban Planning</a><sup id="cite_ref-226" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-226">&#91;222&#93;</a></sup> and UCLouvain\'s Dutch-speaking sister <a href="/wiki/KU_Leuven" title="KU Leuven">Katholieke Universiteit Leuven</a> (KU Leuven)<sup id="cite_ref-227" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-227">&#91;223&#93;</a></sup> (offering bachelor\'s and master\'s degrees in economics &amp; business, law, arts, and architecture; 4,400 students). In addition, the University of Kent\'s <a href="/wiki/Brussels_School_of_International_Studies" title="Brussels School of International Studies">Brussels School of International Studies</a> is a specialised postgraduate school offering advanced international studies.\n</p><p>Also a dozen of university colleges are located in Brussels, including two drama schools, founded in 1832: the French-speaking <a href="/wiki/Conservatoire_royal_de_Bruxelles" class="mw-redirect" title="Conservatoire royal de Bruxelles">Conservatoire Royal</a> and its <a href="/wiki/Dutch_language" title="Dutch language">Dutch-speaking</a> equivalent, the <a href="/wiki/Koninklijk_Conservatorium_(Brussel)" class="mw-redirect" title="Koninklijk Conservatorium (Brussel)">Koninklijk Conservatorium</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-228" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-228">&#91;224&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-229" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-229">&#91;225&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Primary_and_secondary_education">Primary and secondary education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brussels&amp;action=edit&amp;section=45" title="Edit section: Primary and secondary education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Most of Brussels pupils between the ages of 3 and 18 go to schools organised by the <a href="/wiki/French-speaking_Community" class="mw-redirect" title="French-speaking Community">French-speaking Community</a> or the <a href="/wiki/Flemish_Community" title="Flemish Community">Flemish Community</a>, with close to 80% going to French-speaking schools, and roughly 20% to Dutch-speaking schools. Due to the post-war international presence in the city, there are also a number of international schools, including the <a href="/wiki/International_School_of_Brussels" title="International School of Brussels">International School of Brussels</a>, with 1,450 pupils, between the ages of 2<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1020198016">.mw-parser-output .frac{white-space:nowrap}.mw-parser-output .frac .num,.mw-parser-output .frac .den{font-size:80%;line-height:0;vertical-align:super}.mw-parser-output .frac .den{vertical-align:sub}.mw-parser-output .sr-only{border:0;clip:rect(0,0,0,0);height:1px;margin:-1px;overflow:hidden;padding:0;position:absolute;width:1px}</style><span class="frac" role="math"><span class="num">1</span>&#8260;<span class="den">2</span></span> and 18,<sup id="cite_ref-230" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-230">&#91;226&#93;</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/British_School_of_Brussels" title="British School of Brussels">British School of Brussels</a>, and the four <a href="/wiki/European_School" title="European School">European Schools</a>, which provide free education for the children of those working in the <a href="/wiki/Institutions_of_the_European_Union" title="Institutions of the European Union">EU institutions</a>. The combined student population of the four <a href="/wiki/European_School" title="European School">European Schools</a> in Brussels is around 10,000.<sup id="cite_ref-231" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-231">&#91;227&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Libraries">Libraries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brussels&amp;action=edit&amp;section=46" title="Edit section: Libraries">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_libraries_in_Belgium" title="List of libraries in Belgium">List of libraries in Belgium</a></div><p>Brussels has a number of public or private-owned <a href="/wiki/Library" title="Library">libraries</a> on its territory.<sup id="cite_ref-232" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-232">&#91;228&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Libraries in Brussels fall under the competence of the Communities and are usually separated between French-speaking and Dutch-speaking institutions, although some are mixed.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability"><span title="The material near this tag needs to be fact-checked with the cited source(s). (April 2018)">verification needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Science_and_technology">Science and technology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brussels&amp;action=edit&amp;section=47" title="Edit section: Science and technology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Science_and_technology_in_Brussels" title="Science and technology in Brussels">Science and technology in Brussels</a></div>\n<p>Science and technology in Brussels is well developed with the presence of several <a href="/wiki/List_of_universities_in_Belgium" title="List of universities in Belgium">universities</a> and research institutes.\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Museum_of_Natural_Sciences" title="Museum of Natural Sciences">Royal Belgian Institute of Natural Sciences</a> houses the world\'s largest hall completely dedicated to <a href="/wiki/Dinosaur" title="Dinosaur">dinosaurs</a>, with its collection of 30 <a href="/wiki/Fossil" title="Fossil">fossilised</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Iguanodon" title="Iguanodon">Iguanodon</a></i> skeletons.<sup id="cite_ref-233" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-233">&#91;229&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Planetarium_(Belgium)" title="Planetarium (Belgium)">Planetarium</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Observatory_of_Belgium" title="Royal Observatory of Belgium">Royal Observatory of Belgium</a> is one of the largest in Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-234" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-234">&#91;230&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Projet_de_l%27H%C3%B4pital_Erasme_par_MA%C2%B2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Projet_de_l%27H%C3%B4pital_Erasme_par_MA%C2%B2.jpg/220px-Projet_de_l%27H%C3%B4pital_Erasme_par_MA%C2%B2.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Projet_de_l%27H%C3%B4pital_Erasme_par_MA%C2%B2.jpg/330px-Projet_de_l%27H%C3%B4pital_Erasme_par_MA%C2%B2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Projet_de_l%27H%C3%B4pital_Erasme_par_MA%C2%B2.jpg/440px-Projet_de_l%27H%C3%B4pital_Erasme_par_MA%C2%B2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4368" data-file-height="2912" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Projet_de_l%27H%C3%B4pital_Erasme_par_MA%C2%B2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Erasmus_Hospital" title="Erasmus Hospital">Erasmus Hospital</a> in <a href="/wiki/Anderlecht" title="Anderlecht">Anderlecht</a></div></div></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Healthcare">Healthcare</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brussels&amp;action=edit&amp;section=48" title="Edit section: Healthcare">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_hospitals_in_Belgium#Brussels-Capital_Region" title="List of hospitals in Belgium">List of hospitals in Belgium \xc2\xa7&#160;Brussels-Capital Region</a></div>\n<p>Brussels is home to a thriving <a href="/wiki/Pharmaceutical_industry" title="Pharmaceutical industry">pharmaceutical</a> and <a href="/wiki/Health_care" title="Health care">health care</a> industry which includes pioneering <a href="/wiki/Biotechnology" title="Biotechnology">biotechnology</a> research. The health sector employs 70,000 employees in 30,000 companies. There are 3,000 life sciences researchers in the city and two large <a href="/wiki/Science_park" title="Science park">science parks</a>: <a href="/wiki/Da_Vinci_Research_Park" title="Da Vinci Research Park">Da Vinci Research Park</a> and <a href="/wiki/Erasmus_Research_Park" title="Erasmus Research Park">Erasmus Research Park</a>. There are five <a href="/wiki/Teaching_hospital" title="Teaching hospital">university hospitals</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Military_hospital" title="Military hospital">military hospital</a> and more than 40 general hospitals and specialist clinics.<sup id="cite_ref-235" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-235">&#91;231&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Due to <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_Belgium" title="Languages of Belgium">its bilingual nature</a>, hospitals in the <a href="/wiki/Brussels-Capital_Region" class="mw-redirect" title="Brussels-Capital Region">Brussels-Capital Region</a> can be either monolingual French, monolingual Dutch, or bilingual, depending on their nature. University hospitals belong to one of the two <a href="/wiki/Communities,_regions_and_language_areas_of_Belgium" title="Communities, regions and language areas of Belgium">linguistic communities</a> and are thus monolingual French or Dutch by law. Other hospitals managed by a public authority must be legally bilingual. Private hospitals are legally not bound to either language, but most cater to both. However, all hospital emergency services in the Capital Region (whether part of a public or private hospital) are required to be bilingual, since patients transported by emergency <a href="/wiki/Ambulance" title="Ambulance">ambulance</a> cannot chose the hospital they will be brought to.<sup id="cite_ref-236" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-236">&#91;232&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">Transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brussels&amp;action=edit&amp;section=49" title="Edit section: Transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_Brussels" title="Transport in Brussels">Transport in Brussels</a></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Air">Air</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brussels&amp;action=edit&amp;section=50" title="Edit section: Air">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Brussels_Airlines_Airbus_A319_landing_at_Brussels_Airport.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Brussels_Airlines_Airbus_A319_landing_at_Brussels_Airport.jpg/220px-Brussels_Airlines_Airbus_A319_landing_at_Brussels_Airport.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="152" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Brussels_Airlines_Airbus_A319_landing_at_Brussels_Airport.jpg/330px-Brussels_Airlines_Airbus_A319_landing_at_Brussels_Airport.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Brussels_Airlines_Airbus_A319_landing_at_Brussels_Airport.jpg/440px-Brussels_Airlines_Airbus_A319_landing_at_Brussels_Airport.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2536" data-file-height="1754" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Brussels_Airlines_Airbus_A319_landing_at_Brussels_Airport.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Brussels_Airlines" title="Brussels Airlines">Brussels Airlines</a> Airbus A319 landing at <a href="/wiki/Brussels_Airport" title="Brussels Airport">Brussels Airport</a> in <a href="/wiki/Zaventem" title="Zaventem">Zaventem</a></div></div></div>\n<p>The Brussels-Capital Region is served by several airports, all of which are located outside of the administrative territory of the region. The most notable are:\n</p>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Brussels_Airport" title="Brussels Airport">Brussels-National Airport</a>, located in the nearby Flemish municipality of <a href="/wiki/Zaventem" title="Zaventem">Zaventem</a>, 12&#160;km (10&#160;mi) east of the capital;</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Brussels_South_Charleroi_Airport" title="Brussels South Charleroi Airport">Brussels South Charleroi Airport</a>, located in <a href="/wiki/Gosselies" title="Gosselies">Gosselies</a>, a part of the city of <a href="/wiki/Charleroi" title="Charleroi">Charleroi</a> (<a href="/wiki/Wallonia" title="Wallonia">Wallonia</a>), some 50&#160;km (30&#160;mi) south-west of Brussels;</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Melsbroek_Air_Base" title="Melsbroek Air Base">Melsbroek Air Base</a>, located in <a href="/wiki/Steenokkerzeel" title="Steenokkerzeel">Steenokkerzeel</a>, is mainly a military airport and is used in a minority way for civilian travelers.</li></ul>\n<p>The first two are also the main airports of Belgium.<sup id="cite_ref-237" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-237">&#91;233&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Water">Water</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brussels&amp;action=edit&amp;section=51" title="Edit section: Water">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Eug%C3%A8ne_Boudin_005.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Eug%C3%A8ne_Boudin_005.jpg/220px-Eug%C3%A8ne_Boudin_005.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="156" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Eug%C3%A8ne_Boudin_005.jpg/330px-Eug%C3%A8ne_Boudin_005.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Eug%C3%A8ne_Boudin_005.jpg/440px-Eug%C3%A8ne_Boudin_005.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1448" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Eug%C3%A8ne_Boudin_005.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><i>The Saint Catherine Dock</i>, Eug\xc3\xa8ne Boudin (1871)</div></div></div>\n<p>Since the 16th century, Brussels has had its own harbour, the <a href="/wiki/Port_of_Brussels" title="Port of Brussels">port of Brussels</a>. It has been enlarged throughout the centuries to become the second Belgian inland port. Historically situated near the <span lang="fr" style="font-style: normal;" title="French-language text">Place Sainte-Catherine</span>/<span lang="nl" style="font-style: normal;" title="Dutch-language text">Sint-Katelijneplein</span>, it lies today to the northwest of the region, on the <a href="/wiki/Brussels%E2%80%93Scheldt_Maritime_Canal" title="Brussels\xe2\x80\x93Scheldt Maritime Canal">Brussels\xe2\x80\x93Scheldt Maritime Canal</a> (commonly called Willebroek Canal), which connects Brussels to <a href="/wiki/Antwerp" title="Antwerp">Antwerp</a> via the <a href="/wiki/Scheldt" title="Scheldt">Scheldt</a>. Ships and large barges up to 4,500 tons can penetrate deep into the country, avoiding break-ups and load transfers between Antwerp and the centre of Brussels, hence reducing the cost for companies using the canal, and thus offering a competitive advantage.\n</p><p>Moreover, the connection of the Willebroek Canal with the <a href="/wiki/Brussels%E2%80%93Charleroi_Canal" title="Brussels\xe2\x80\x93Charleroi Canal">Brussels\xe2\x80\x93Charleroi Canal</a>, in the very heart of the capital, creates a north\xe2\x80\x93south link, by means of waterways, between the Netherlands, Flanders and the industrial zone of <a href="/wiki/Hainaut_(province)" class="mw-redirect" title="Hainaut (province)">Hainaut</a> (<a href="/wiki/Wallonia" title="Wallonia">Wallonia</a>). There, navigation can access the network of French canals, thanks to the important <a href="/wiki/Canal_inclined_plane" title="Canal inclined plane">inclined plane</a> of <a href="/wiki/Ronqui%C3%A8res_inclined_plane" title="Ronqui\xc3\xa8res inclined plane">Ronqui\xc3\xa8res</a> and the lifts of <a href="/wiki/Str%C3%A9py-Bracquegnies" title="Str\xc3\xa9py-Bracquegnies">Str\xc3\xa9py-Bracquegnies</a>.\n</p><p>The importance of river traffic in Brussels makes it possible to avoid the road equivalent of 740,000 trucks per year\xe2\x80\x94almost 2,000 per day\xe2\x80\x94which, in addition to easing traffic problems, represents an estimated carbon dioxide saving of 51,545 tonnes per year.<sup id="cite_ref-238" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-238">&#91;234&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Train">Train</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brussels&amp;action=edit&amp;section=52" title="Edit section: Train">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/List_of_railway_stations_in_Belgium" class="mw-redirect" title="List of railway stations in Belgium">List of railway stations in Belgium</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Gare_de_Bruxelles-Midi_Station_Brussel-Zuid.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Gare_de_Bruxelles-Midi_Station_Brussel-Zuid.jpg/220px-Gare_de_Bruxelles-Midi_Station_Brussel-Zuid.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="132" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Gare_de_Bruxelles-Midi_Station_Brussel-Zuid.jpg/330px-Gare_de_Bruxelles-Midi_Station_Brussel-Zuid.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Gare_de_Bruxelles-Midi_Station_Brussel-Zuid.jpg/440px-Gare_de_Bruxelles-Midi_Station_Brussel-Zuid.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="960" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Gare_de_Bruxelles-Midi_Station_Brussel-Zuid.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Main hall of <a href="/wiki/Brussels-South_railway_station" title="Brussels-South railway station">Brussels-South railway station</a>, home to the <a href="/wiki/Eurostar" title="Eurostar">Eurostar</a> train service to <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a></div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ice_bruxelles.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Ice_bruxelles.JPG/220px-Ice_bruxelles.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Ice_bruxelles.JPG/330px-Ice_bruxelles.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Ice_bruxelles.JPG/440px-Ice_bruxelles.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2400" data-file-height="1600" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ice_bruxelles.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>High-speed rail networks connect Brussels with other European cities (<a href="/wiki/Intercity_Express" title="Intercity Express">ICE</a> train in the <a href="/wiki/Brussels-North_railway_station" title="Brussels-North railway station">North Station</a> pictured).</div></div></div>\n<p>The Brussels-Capital Region has three main train stations: <a href="/wiki/Brussels-South_railway_station" title="Brussels-South railway station">Brussels-South</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brussels-Central_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Brussels-Central railway station">Brussels-Central</a> and <a href="/wiki/Brussels-North_railway_station" title="Brussels-North railway station">Brussels-North</a>, which are also the busiest of the country.<sup id="cite_ref-:2_33-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-33">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> Brussels-South is also served by direct high-speed rail links: to <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a> by <a href="/wiki/Eurostar" title="Eurostar">Eurostar</a> trains via the <a href="/wiki/Channel_Tunnel" title="Channel Tunnel">Channel Tunnel</a> (1hr 51min); to <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam" title="Amsterdam">Amsterdam</a><sup id="cite_ref-239" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-239">&#91;235&#93;</a></sup> by <a href="/wiki/Thalys" title="Thalys">Thalys</a> and <i>InterCity</i> connections; to Amsterdam, <a href="/wiki/Paris" title="Paris">Paris</a> (1hr 50min and 1hr 25min respectively as of 6&#160;April&#160;2015<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Brussels&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>), and <a href="/wiki/Cologne" title="Cologne">Cologne</a> by <a href="/wiki/Thalys" title="Thalys">Thalys</a>; and to Cologne (1hr 50min) and <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt" title="Frankfurt">Frankfurt</a> (2hr 57min) by the German <a href="/wiki/Intercity_Express" title="Intercity Express">ICE</a>.\n</p><p>The train rails in Brussels go underground, near the centre, through the <a href="/wiki/North%E2%80%93South_connection" title="North\xe2\x80\x93South connection">North\xe2\x80\x93South connection</a>, with Brussels Central Station also being largely underground. The tunnel itself is only six tracks wide at its narrowest point, which often causes congestion and delays due to heavy use of the route.\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/City_of_Brussels" title="City of Brussels">City of Brussels</a> has minor railway stations at <a href="/wiki/Bockstael_railway_station" title="Bockstael railway station">Bockstael</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brussels-Chapel_railway_station" title="Brussels-Chapel railway station">Brussels-Chapel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brussels-Congres_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Brussels-Congres railway station">Brussels-Congres</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brussels-Luxembourg_railway_station" title="Brussels-Luxembourg railway station">Brussels-Luxembourg</a>, <a href="/wiki/Schuman_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Schuman station">Brussels-Schuman</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brussels-West_station" title="Brussels-West station">Brussels-West</a>, <a href="/wiki/Haren_railway_station_(Brussels)" title="Haren railway station (Brussels)">Haren</a>, <a href="/wiki/Haren-South_railway_station" title="Haren-South railway station">Haren-South</a> and <a href="/wiki/Simonis_metro_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Simonis metro station">Simonis</a>. In the Brussels Region, there are also railways stations at <a href="/wiki/Berchem-Sainte-Agathe_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Berchem-Sainte-Agathe railway station">Berchem-Sainte-Agathe</a>, <a href="/wiki/Boitsfort_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Boitsfort railway station">Boitsfort</a>, <a href="/wiki/Boondael_railway_station" title="Boondael railway station">Boondael</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bordet_railway_station" title="Bordet railway station">Bordet (Evere)</a>, <a href="/wiki/Etterbeek_railway_station" title="Etterbeek railway station">Etterbeek</a>, <a href="/wiki/Evere_railway_station" title="Evere railway station">Evere</a>, <a href="/wiki/Forest-East_railway_station" title="Forest-East railway station">Forest-East</a>, <a href="/wiki/Forest-South_railway_station" title="Forest-South railway station">Forest-South</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jette_railway_station" title="Jette railway station">Jette</a>, <a href="/wiki/Meiser_railway_station" title="Meiser railway station">Meiser (Schaerbeek)</a>, <a href="/wiki/Moensberg_railway_station" title="Moensberg railway station">Moensberg (Uccle)</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saint-Job_railway_station" title="Saint-Job railway station">Saint-Job (Uccle)</a>, <a href="/wiki/Schaerbeek_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Schaerbeek railway station">Schaarbeek</a>, <a href="/wiki/Uccle-Calevoet_railway_station" title="Uccle-Calevoet railway station">Uccle-Calevoet</a>, <a href="/wiki/Uccle-Stalle_railway_station" title="Uccle-Stalle railway station">Uccle-Stalle</a>, Vivier d\'Oie-Diesdelle (Uccle), <a href="/wiki/Merode_station" title="Merode station">Merode</a> and <a href="/wiki/Watermael_railway_station" title="Watermael railway station">Watermael</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="City_public_transport">City public transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brussels&amp;action=edit&amp;section=53" title="Edit section: City public transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The Brussels Intercommunal Transport Company (<a href="/wiki/Brussels_Intercommunal_Transport_Company" title="Brussels Intercommunal Transport Company">STIB/MIVB</a>) is the local <a href="/wiki/Public_transport" title="Public transport">public transport</a> operator in Brussels. It covers the 19 municipalities of the Brussels-Capital Region and some surface routes extend to the near suburbs in the other two regions.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Metro">Metro</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brussels&amp;action=edit&amp;section=54" title="Edit section: Metro">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Rame_%22Boa%22.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Rame_%22Boa%22.jpg/220px-Rame_%22Boa%22.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Rame_%22Boa%22.jpg/330px-Rame_%22Boa%22.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Rame_%22Boa%22.jpg/440px-Rame_%22Boa%22.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3872" data-file-height="2592" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Rame_%22Boa%22.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Brussels_metro" class="mw-redirect" title="Brussels metro">Brussels metro</a> carriage at <a href="/wiki/Erasmus_metro_station" title="Erasmus metro station">Erasme/Erasmus metro station</a></div></div></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Brussels_metro" class="mw-redirect" title="Brussels metro">Brussels metro</a> dates back to 1976,<sup id="cite_ref-240" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-240">&#91;236&#93;</a></sup> but underground lines known as the <a href="/wiki/Brussels_premetro" class="mw-redirect" title="Brussels premetro"><i>premetro</i></a> have been serviced by tramways since 1968. It is the only <a href="/wiki/Rapid_transit" title="Rapid transit">rapid transit</a> system in Belgium (<a href="/wiki/Antwerp_Pre-metro" title="Antwerp Pre-metro">Antwerp</a> and <a href="/wiki/Charleroi_Metro" title="Charleroi Metro">Charleroi</a> both having <a href="/wiki/Light_rail" title="Light rail">light rail</a> systems). The network consists of four conventional metro lines and three <i>premetro</i> lines. The metro-grade lines are M1, M2, M5, and M6, with some shared sections, covering a total of 40&#160;km (25&#160;mi).<sup id="cite_ref-The_network_and_vehicles_241-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_network_and_vehicles-241">&#91;237&#93;</a></sup> As of 2017<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Brussels&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, the metro network within the region has a total of 69 metro and <i>premetro</i> stations. The metro is an important <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_Brussels" title="Transport in Brussels">means of transport</a>, connecting with six <a href="/wiki/Railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Railway station">railway stations</a> of the <a href="/wiki/National_Railway_Company_of_Belgium" title="National Railway Company of Belgium">National Railway Company of Belgium</a> (NMBS/SNCB), and many tram and bus stops operated by STIB/MIVB, and with <a href="/wiki/Flanders" title="Flanders">Flemish</a> <a href="/wiki/De_Lijn" title="De Lijn">De Lijn</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wallonia" title="Wallonia">Walloon</a> <a href="/wiki/TEC_(transport)" class="mw-redirect" title="TEC (transport)">TEC</a> bus stops.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Trams_and_buses">Trams and buses</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brussels&amp;action=edit&amp;section=55" title="Edit section: Trams and buses">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>A comprehensive <a href="/wiki/Brussels_buses" title="Brussels buses">bus</a> and <a href="/wiki/Brussels_trams" class="mw-redirect" title="Brussels trams">tram network</a> covers the region. As of 2017<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Brussels&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, the Brussels tram system consists of 17 tram lines (three of which \xe2\x80\x93 lines T3, T4 and T7 \xe2\x80\x93 qualify as <i>premetro</i> lines). The total route length is 139&#160;km (86&#160;mi),<sup id="cite_ref-The_network_and_vehicles_241-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_network_and_vehicles-241">&#91;237&#93;</a></sup> making it one of the largest tram networks in Europe. The Brussels bus network is complementary to the rail network. It consists of 50 bus routes and 11 night routes, spanning 445&#160;km (277&#160;mi).<sup id="cite_ref-The_network_and_vehicles_241-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_network_and_vehicles-241">&#91;237&#93;</a></sup> Since April 2007, STIB/MIVB has been operating a night bus network called Noctis. On Fridays and Saturdays, 11 bus routes operate from midnight until 3 a.m. They run from the centre of Brussels to the outer reaches of the Brussels-Capital Region.<sup id="cite_ref-242" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-242">&#91;238&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Ticketing">Ticketing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brussels&amp;action=edit&amp;section=56" title="Edit section: Ticketing">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>An interticketing system means that a STIB/MIVB ticket holder can use the train or long-distance buses inside the region. A single journey can include multiple stages across the different modes of transport. The commuter services operated by <a href="/wiki/De_Lijn" title="De Lijn">De Lijn</a>, <a href="/wiki/TEC_(transport)" class="mw-redirect" title="TEC (transport)">TEC</a> and <a href="/wiki/National_Railway_Company_of_Belgium" title="National Railway Company of Belgium">NMBS/SNCB</a> will, in the next few years,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="The time period mentioned near this tag is ambiguous. (September 2016)">when?</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> be augmented by the <a href="/wiki/Brussels_Regional_Express_Network" title="Brussels Regional Express Network">Brussels Regional Express Network</a> (RER/GEN), which will connect the capital and surrounding towns. Since August 2016, paper tickets have been discontinued in favour of electronic MoBIB cards.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_public_transport">Other public transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brussels&amp;action=edit&amp;section=57" title="Edit section: Other public transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:VilloStationAlmostFull.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/VilloStationAlmostFull.jpg/220px-VilloStationAlmostFull.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="177" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/VilloStationAlmostFull.jpg/330px-VilloStationAlmostFull.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/VilloStationAlmostFull.jpg/440px-VilloStationAlmostFull.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2868" data-file-height="2304" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:VilloStationAlmostFull.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><i><a href="/wiki/Villo!" title="Villo!">Villo!</a></i> bicycles in Brussels</div></div></div><p>Since 2003, Brussels has had a car-sharing service operated by the <a href="/wiki/Bremen" title="Bremen">Bremen</a> company Cambio, in partnership with the STIB/MIVB and local ridesharing company Taxi Stop. In 2006, a <a href="/wiki/Community_bicycle_program" class="mw-redirect" title="Community bicycle program">public bicycle-sharing programme</a> was introduced. The scheme was subsequently taken over by <a href="/wiki/Villo!" title="Villo!">Villo!</a>. Since 2008, this night-time public transport service has been supplemented by Collecto, a shared taxi system, which operates on weekdays between 11 p.m. and 6 a.m. In 2012, the Zen Car electric car-sharing scheme was launched in the university and European areas.\n</p><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Road_network">Road network</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brussels&amp;action=edit&amp;section=58" title="Edit section: Road network">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Wetstraat.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Wetstraat.jpg/170px-Wetstraat.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Wetstraat.jpg/255px-Wetstraat.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Wetstraat.jpg/340px-Wetstraat.jpg 2x" data-file-width="480" data-file-height="640" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Wetstraat.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Rue_de_la_Loi" title="Rue de la Loi">Rue de la Loi/Wetstraat</a> is one of the city\'s main streets.</div></div></div>\n<p>In medieval times, Brussels stood at the intersection of routes running north\xe2\x80\x93south (the modern <span lang="fr" style="font-style: normal;" title="French-language text">Rue Haute</span>/<span lang="nl" style="font-style: normal;" title="Dutch-language text">Hoogstraat</span>) and east\xe2\x80\x93west (<span lang="fr" style="font-style: normal;" title="French-language text">Chauss\xc3\xa9e de Gand</span>/<span lang="nl" style="font-style: normal;" title="Dutch-language text">Gentsesteenweg</span>-<span lang="fr" style="font-style: normal;" title="French-language text">Rue du March\xc3\xa9 aux Herbes</span>/<span lang="nl" style="font-style: normal;" title="Dutch-language text">Grasmarkt</span>-<span lang="fr" style="font-style: normal;" title="French-language text">Rue de Namur</span>/<span lang="nl" style="font-style: normal;" title="Dutch-language text">Naamsestraat</span>). The ancient pattern of streets, radiating from the <a href="/wiki/Grand_Place" title="Grand Place">Grand Place</a>, in large part remains, but has been overlaid by <a href="/wiki/Central_Boulevards_of_Brussels" title="Central Boulevards of Brussels">boulevards</a> built <a href="/wiki/Covering_of_the_Senne" title="Covering of the Senne">over the River Senne</a>, <a href="/wiki/Small_ring_(Brussels)" title="Small ring (Brussels)">over the city walls</a> and over the railway connection between the North and South Stations.\n</p><p>Today, Brussels has the most congested traffic in North America and Europe, according to US traffic information platform <a href="/wiki/INRIX" title="INRIX">INRIX</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-243" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-243">&#91;239&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<table class="infobox" style="float:right;">\n<caption>Distances to other cities\n</caption>\n<tbody><tr>\n<td>These distances are <a
