title="London">London</a></td>\n<td>320.7&#160;km (199.3&#160;mi) W\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>Brussels is the hub of a range of old national roads, the main ones being clockwise: the <a href="/wiki/N1_road_(Belgium)" title="N1 road (Belgium)">N1</a> (N to <a href="/wiki/Breda" title="Breda">Breda</a>), <a href="/wiki/N2_road_(Belgium)" title="N2 road (Belgium)">N2</a> (E to <a href="/wiki/Maastricht" title="Maastricht">Maastricht</a>), <a href="/wiki/N3_road_(Belgium)" title="N3 road (Belgium)">N3</a> (E to <a href="/wiki/Aachen" title="Aachen">Aachen</a>), <a href="/wiki/N4_road_(Belgium)" title="N4 road (Belgium)">N4</a> (SE to <a href="/wiki/Luxembourg_City" title="Luxembourg City">Luxembourg</a>) <a href="/wiki/N5_road_(Belgium)" title="N5 road (Belgium)">N5</a> (S to <a href="/wiki/Reims" title="Reims">Rheims</a>), N6 (S to <a href="/wiki/Maubeuge" title="Maubeuge">Maubeuge</a>), N7 (SW to <a href="/wiki/Lille" title="Lille">Lille</a>), <a href="/wiki/N8_road_(Belgium)" title="N8 road (Belgium)">N8</a> (W to <a href="/wiki/Koksijde" title="Koksijde">Koksijde</a>) and N9 (NW to <a href="/wiki/Ostend" title="Ostend">Ostend</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-244" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-244">&#91;240&#93;</a></sup> Usually named <i lang="fr" title="French-language text">chauss\xc3\xa9es</i>/<i lang="nl" title="Dutch-language text">steenwegen</i>, these highways normally run in a straight line, but sometimes lose themselves in a maze of narrow shopping streets.\n</p><p>The region is skirted by the <a href="/wiki/European_route_E19" title="European route E19">European route E19</a> (N-S) and the <a href="/wiki/European_route_E40" title="European route E40">E40</a> (E-W), while the <a href="/wiki/E411" class="mw-redirect" title="E411">E411</a> leads away to the SE. Brussels has an <a href="/wiki/Beltway" class="mw-redirect" title="Beltway">orbital motorway</a>, numbered R0 (R-zero) and commonly referred to as the <i>Ring</i>. It is pear-shaped, as the southern side was never built as originally conceived, owing to residents\' objections.\n</p><p>The city centre, sometimes known as the <i>Pentagon</i>, is surrounded by an inner ring road, the <a href="/wiki/Small_ring_(Brussels)" title="Small ring (Brussels)"><i>Small Ring</i></a> (French: <i lang="fr" title="French-language text">Petite Ceinture</i>, Dutch: <i lang="nl" title="Dutch-language text">Kleine Ring</i>), a sequence of boulevards formally numbered R20 or N0. These were built upon the site of the <a href="/wiki/Second_walls_of_Brussels" class="mw-redirect" title="Second walls of Brussels">second set of city walls</a> following their demolition. The <a href="/wiki/Brussels_Metro_line_2" title="Brussels Metro line 2">metro line 2</a> runs under much of these. Since June 2015, a number of <a href="/wiki/Central_Boulevards_of_Brussels" title="Central Boulevards of Brussels">central boulevards</a> inside the <i>Pentagon</i> have become car-free, limiting transit traffic through the old city.<sup id="cite_ref-245" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-245">&#91;241&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On the eastern side of the region, the R21 or <i><a href="/wiki/Greater_ring_(Brussels)" title="Greater ring (Brussels)">Greater Ring</a></i> (French: <i lang="fr" title="French-language text">Grande Ceinture</i>, Dutch: <i lang="nl" title="Dutch-language text">Grote Ring</i>) is formed by a string of boulevards that curves round from <a href="/wiki/Laeken" title="Laeken">Laeken</a> to <a href="/wiki/Uccle" title="Uccle">Uccle</a>. Some <i>premetro</i> stations (see <a href="/wiki/Brussels_metro" class="mw-redirect" title="Brussels metro">Brussels metro</a>) were built on that route. A little further out, a stretch numbered R22 leads from Zaventem to <a href="/wiki/Uccle" title="Uccle">Saint-Job</a>.\n</p>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Security_and_emergency_services">Security and emergency services</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brussels&amp;action=edit&amp;section=59" title="Edit section: Security and emergency services">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Police">Police</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brussels&amp;action=edit&amp;section=60" title="Edit section: Police">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Law_enforcement_in_Belgium" title="Law enforcement in Belgium">Law enforcement in Belgium</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:EPP_Summit_March_2012_(48).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/EPP_Summit_March_2012_%2848%29.jpg/220px-EPP_Summit_March_2012_%2848%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/EPP_Summit_March_2012_%2848%29.jpg/330px-EPP_Summit_March_2012_%2848%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/EPP_Summit_March_2012_%2848%29.jpg/440px-EPP_Summit_March_2012_%2848%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2128" data-file-height="1416" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:EPP_Summit_March_2012_(48).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Policeman in Brussels</div></div></div>\n<p>The Brussels local <a href="/wiki/Police" title="Police">police</a>, supported by the federal police, is responsible for law enforcement in Brussels. The 19 municipalities of the Brussels-Capital Region are divided into six police zones,<sup id="cite_ref-246" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-246">&#91;242&#93;</a></sup> all bilingual (French and Dutch):\n</p>\n<ul><li>5339 Brussels Capital Ixelles: the <a href="/wiki/City_of_Brussels" title="City of Brussels">City of Brussels</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ixelles" title="Ixelles">Ixelles</a></li>\n<li>5340 Brussels West: <a href="/wiki/Sint-Agatha-Berchem" title="Sint-Agatha-Berchem">Berchem-Sainte-Agathe</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ganshoren" title="Ganshoren">Ganshoren</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jette" title="Jette">Jette</a>, <a href="/wiki/Koekelberg" title="Koekelberg">Koekelberg</a> and <a href="/wiki/Molenbeek-Saint-Jean" title="Molenbeek-Saint-Jean">Molenbeek-Saint-Jean</a></li>\n<li>5341 South: <a href="/wiki/Anderlecht" title="Anderlecht">Anderlecht</a>, <a href="/wiki/Forest,_Belgium" title="Forest, Belgium">Forest</a> and <a href="/wiki/Saint-Gilles,_Belgium" title="Saint-Gilles, Belgium">Saint-Gilles</a></li>\n<li>5342 Uccle/Watermael-Boitsfort/Auderghem: <a href="/wiki/Auderghem" title="Auderghem">Auderghem</a>, <a href="/wiki/Uccle" title="Uccle">Uccle</a> and <a href="/wiki/Watermael-Boitsfort" title="Watermael-Boitsfort">Watermael-Boitsfort</a></li>\n<li>5343 Montgomery: <a href="/wiki/Etterbeek" title="Etterbeek">Etterbeek</a>, <a href="/wiki/Woluwe-Saint-Lambert" title="Woluwe-Saint-Lambert">Woluwe-Saint-Lambert</a> et <a href="/wiki/Woluwe-Saint-Pierre" title="Woluwe-Saint-Pierre">Woluwe-Saint-Pierre</a></li>\n<li>5344 Polbruno: <a href="/wiki/Evere" title="Evere">Evere</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saint-Josse-ten-Noode" title="Saint-Josse-ten-Noode">Saint-Josse-ten-Noode</a> et <a href="/wiki/Schaerbeek" title="Schaerbeek">Schaerbeek</a></li></ul>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Fire_department">Fire department</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brussels&amp;action=edit&amp;section=61" title="Edit section: Fire department">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The Brussels Fire and Emergency Medical Care Service, commonly known by its acronym SIAMU (DBDMH), operates in the 19 municipalities of Brussels.<sup id="cite_ref-247" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-247">&#91;243&#93;</a></sup> It is a class X fire department and the largest <a href="/wiki/Fire_department" title="Fire department">fire service</a> in Belgium in terms of annual operations, equipment, and personnel. It has 9 <a href="/wiki/Fire_station" title="Fire station">fire stations</a>, spread over the entire Brussels-Capital Region, and employs about 1,000 professional <a href="/wiki/Firefighter" title="Firefighter">firefighters</a>. As well as preventing and fighting fires, SIAMU also provides emergency medical care services in Brussels via its centralised 100 number (and the single 112 emergency number for the 27 countries of the European Union). It is bilingual (French\xe2\x80\x93Dutch).\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Parks_and_green_spaces">Parks and green spaces</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brussels&amp;action=edit&amp;section=62" title="Edit section: Parks and green spaces">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_parks_and_gardens_in_Brussels" title="List of parks and gardens in Brussels">List of parks and gardens in Brussels</a></div>\n<p>Brussels is one of the greenest capitals in Europe, with over 8,000 hectares of green spaces.<sup id="cite_ref-248" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-248">&#91;244&#93;</a></sup> Vegetation cover and natural areas are higher in the outskirts, where they have limited the <a href="/wiki/Peri-urbanisation" title="Peri-urbanisation">peri-urbanisation</a> of the capital, but they decrease sharply towards the centre of Brussels; 10% in the central <i>Pentagon</i>, 30% of the municipalities in the first ring, and 71% of the municipalities in the second ring are occupied by green spaces.\n</p><p>Many parks and gardens, both public and privately owned, are scattered throughout the city. In addition to this, the <a href="/wiki/Sonian_Forest" title="Sonian Forest">Sonian Forest</a> is located in its southern part and stretches out over the three <a href="/wiki/Communities,_regions_and_language_areas_of_Belgium#Regions" title="Communities, regions and language areas of Belgium">Belgian regions</a>. As of 2017<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Brussels&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, it has been inscribed as a <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a> <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Site" title="World Heritage Site">World Heritage Site</a>, the only Belgian component to the multinational inscription \'<a href="/wiki/Primeval_Beech_Forests_of_the_Carpathians_and_Other_Regions_of_Europe" class="mw-redirect" title="Primeval Beech Forests of the Carpathians and Other Regions of Europe">Primeval Beech Forests of the Carpathians and Other Regions of Europe</a>\'.\n</p>\n<ul class="gallery mw-gallery-packed">\n\t\t<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 215.33333333333px"><div style="width: id="Notable_people">Notable people</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brussels&amp;action=edit&amp;section=63" title="Edit section: Notable people">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_people_from_Brussels" title="List of people from Brussels">List of people from Brussels</a></div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="International_relations">International relations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brussels&amp;action=edit&amp;section=64" title="Edit section: International relations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Twin_towns_and_sister_cities">Twin towns and sister cities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brussels&amp;action=edit&amp;section=65" title="Edit section: Twin towns and sister cities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_twin_towns_and_sister_cities_in_Belgium" title="List of twin towns and sister cities in Belgium">List of twin towns and sister cities in Belgium</a></div>\n<p>Brussels is <a href="/wiki/Sister_city" title="Sister city">twinned</a> with the following cities:\n</p>\n<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r998391716">.mw-parser-output .div-col{margin-top:0.3em;column-width:30em}.mw-parser-output .div-col-small{font-size:90%}.mw-parser-output .div-col-rules{column-rule:1px solid #aaa}.mw-parser-output .div-col dl,.mw-parser-output .div-col ol,.mw-parser-output .div-col ul{margin-top:0}.mw-parser-output .div-col li,.mw-parser-output .div-col dd{page-break-inside:avoid;break-inside:avoid-column}</style><div class="div-col" Hoofdstedelijk Gewest.ogg">listen</a></span></span>)</span><small>. <i>Gewest</i> in isolation is</small> <small>pronounced&#32;</small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Dutch" title="Help:IPA/Dutch">[\xc9\xa3\xc9\x99\xcb\x88\xca\x8b\xc9\x9bst]</a></span>&#32;<span class="nowrap" style="font-size:85%">(<span See <a href="#European_Union">the section dedicated to this issue</a>.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-155"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-155">^</a></b></span> <span The metropolitan area of Brussels is divided into three levels. First, the central agglomeration (<i>geoperationaliseerde agglomeratie</i>) with 1,451,047 inhabitants (2008-01-01, adjusted to municipal borders). Adding the closest surroundings (suburbs, <i>banlieue</i> or <i>buitenwijken</i>) gives a total of 1,831,496.
